<bookmarkvalue>N function</bookmarkvalue>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCN">Returns the numeric value of the given parameter. Returns 0 if parameter is text or FALSE.</ahelp>
If an error occurs the function returns the error value.
N(Value)
<emph>Value</emph> is the parameter to be converted into a number. N() returns the numeric value if it can. It returns the logical values TRUE and FALSE as 1 and 0 respectively. It returns text as 0.
<item type="input">=N(123)</item> returns 123
<item type="input">=N(TRUE())</item> returns 1
<item type="input">=N(FALSE())</item> returns 0
<item type="input">=N("abc")</item> returns 0
=N(1/0) returns #DIV/0!
<bookmarkvalue>NA function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>#N/A error;assigning to a cell</bookmarkvalue>
NA
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCNV">Returns the error value #N/A.</ahelp>
NA()
<item type="input">=NA()</item> converts the contents of the cell into #N/A.
<bookmarkvalue>TYPE function</bookmarkvalue>
TYPE
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCTYP">Returns the type of value, where 1 = number, 2 = text, 4 = Boolean value, 8 = formula, 16 = error value, 64 = array.</ahelp>
TYPE(Value)
<emph>Value</emph> is a specific value for which the data type is determined.
Example (see example table above)
<item type="input">=TYPE(C2)</item> returns 2 as a result.
<item type="input">=TYPE(D9)</item> returns 1 as a result.
<bookmarkvalue>CELL function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>cell information</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>information on cells</bookmarkvalue>
CELL
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZELLE">Returns information on address, formatting or contents of a cell.</ahelp>
CELL("InfoType" [; Reference])
<emph>InfoType</emph> is the character string that specifies the type of information. The character string is always in English. Upper or lower case is optional.
InfoType
Meaning
Returns the number of the referenced column.
<item type="input">=CELL("COL";D2)</item> returns 4.
Returns the number of the referenced row.
<item type="input">=CELL("ROW";D2)</item> returns 2.
Returns the number of the referenced sheet.
<item type="input">=CELL("Sheet";Sheet3.D2)</item> returns 3.
Returns the absolute address of the referenced cell.
<item type="input">=CELL("ADDRESS";D2)</item> returns $D$2.
<item type="input">=CELL("ADDRESS";Sheet3.D2)</item> returns $Sheet3.$D$2.
<item type="input">=CELL("ADDRESS";'X:\dr\test.ods'#$Sheet1.D2)</item> returns 'file:///X:/dr/test.ods'#$Sheet1.$D$2.
Returns the file name and the sheet number of the referenced cell.
<item type="input">=CELL("FILENAME";D2)</item> returns 'file:///X:/dr/own.ods'#$Sheet1, if the formula in the current document X:\dr\own.ods is located in Sheet1.
<item type="input">=CELL("FILENAME";'X:\dr\test.ods'#$Sheet1.D2)</item> returns 'file:///X:/dr/test.ods'#$Sheet1.
Returns the complete cell address in Lotus™ notation.
<item type="input">=CELL("COORD"; D2)</item> returns $A:$D$2.
<item type="input">=CELL("COORD"; Sheet3.D2)</item> returns $C:$D$2.
Returns the contents of the referenced cell, without any formatting.
Returns the type of cell contents.
b = blank. empty cell
l = label. Text, result of a formula as text
v = value. Value, result of a formula as a number
Returns the width of the referenced column. The unit is the number of zeros (0) that fit into the column in the default text and the default size.
Returns the alignment of the referenced cell.
' = align left or left-justified
" = align right
^ = centered
\ = repeating (currently inactive)
Returns the status of the cell protection for the cell.
1 = cell is protected
0 = cell is not protected
Returns a character string that indicates the number format.
, = number with thousands separator
F = number without thousands separator
C = currency format
S = exponential representation, for example, 1.234+E56
P = percentage
In the above formats, the number of decimal places after the decimal separator is given as a number. Example: the number format #,##0.0 returns ,1 and the number format 00.000% returns P3
D1 = MMM-D-YY, MM-D-YY and similar formats
G = All other formats
- (Minus) at the end = negative numbers are formatted in color
() (brackets) at the end = there is an opening bracket in the format code
Returns 1, if negative values have been formatted in color, otherwise 0.
Returns 1 if the format code contains an opening bracket (, otherwise 0.
<emph>Reference</emph> (list of options) is the position of the cell to be examined. If <emph>Reference</emph> is a range, the cell moves to the top left of the range. If <emph>Reference</emph> is missing, $[officename] Calc uses the position of the cell in which this formula is located. Microsoft Excel uses the reference of the cell in which the cursor is positioned.
Logical Functions
<bookmarkvalue>logical functions</bookmarkvalue>      <bookmarkvalue>Function Wizard; logical</bookmarkvalue>      <bookmarkvalue>functions; logical functions</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="logicaltext">This category contains the <emph>Logical</emph> functions.</variable>
Handling non-logical arguments in logical functions
Zero (0) is equivalent to FALSE and all other numbers are equivalent to TRUE.
Empty cells and text in cells are ignored.
A #VALUE error is raised if all arguments are ignored.
A #VALUE error is raised if one argument is direct text (not text in a cell).
Errors as argument lead to an error.
<bookmarkvalue>AND function</bookmarkvalue>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCUND">Returns TRUE if all arguments are TRUE.</ahelp> If one of the elements is FALSE, this function returns the FALSE value.
The arguments are either logical expressions themselves (TRUE, 1<5, 2+3=7, B8<10) that return logical values, or arrays (A1:C3) containing logical values.
The logical values of entries 12<13; 14>12, and 7<6 are to be checked:
<item type="input">=AND(12<13;14>12;7<6)</item> returns FALSE.
<item type="input">=AND (FALSE;TRUE)</item> returns FALSE.
<bookmarkvalue>FALSE function</bookmarkvalue>
FALSE
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCFALSCH">Returns the logical value FALSE.</ahelp> The FALSE() function does not require any arguments, and always returns the logical value FALSE.
FALSE()
<item type="input">=FALSE()</item> returns FALSE
<item type="input">=NOT(FALSE())</item> returns TRUE
<bookmarkvalue>IF function</bookmarkvalue>
IF
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCWENN">Specifies a logical test to be performed.</ahelp>
IF(Test [; ThenValue [; OtherwiseValue]])
<emph>Test</emph> is any value or expression that can be TRUE or FALSE.
<emph>ThenValue</emph> (optional) is the value that is returned if the logical test is TRUE.
<emph>OtherwiseValue</emph> (optional) is the value that is returned if the logical test is FALSE.
<item type="input">=IF(A1>5;100;"too small")</item> If the value in A1 is higher than 5, the value 100 is entered in the current cell; otherwise, the text “too small” (without quotes) is entered.
<bookmarkvalue>NOT function</bookmarkvalue>
NOT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCNICHT">Complements (inverts) a logical value.</ahelp>
NOT(LogicalValue)
<emph>LogicalValue</emph> is any value to be complemented.
<item type="input">=NOT(A)</item>. If A=TRUE then NOT(A) will evaluate FALSE.
<bookmarkvalue>OR function</bookmarkvalue>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCODER">Returns TRUE if at least one argument is TRUE.</ahelp> This function returns the value FALSE, if all the arguments have the logical value FALSE.
The logical values of entries 12<11; 13>22, and 45=45 are to be checked.
<item type="input">=OR(12<11;13>22;45=45)</item> returns TRUE.
<item type="input">=OR(FALSE;TRUE)</item> returns TRUE.
<bookmarkvalue>TRUE function</bookmarkvalue>
TRUE
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCWAHR">The logical value is set to TRUE.</ahelp> The TRUE() function does not require any arguments, and always returns the logical value TRUE.
TRUE()
If A=TRUE and B=FALSE the following examples appear:
<item type="input">=AND(A;B)</item> returns FALSE
<item type="input">=OR(A;B)</item> returns TRUE
<item type="input">=NOT(AND(A;B))</item> returns TRUE
<bookmarkvalue>XOR function</bookmarkvalue>
XOR
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCXOR">Returns true if an odd number of arguments evaluates to TRUE.</ahelp>
<item type="input">=XOR(TRUE;TRUE)</item> returns FALSE
<item type="input">=XOR(TRUE;TRUE;TRUE)</item> returns TRUE
<item type="input">=XOR(FALSE;TRUE)</item> returns TRUE
Mathematical Functions
<bookmarkvalue>mathematical functions</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>Function Wizard; mathematical</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>functions; mathematical functions</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>trigonometric functions</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="mathematiktext">This category contains the <emph>Mathematical</emph> functions for Calc.</variable> To open the <emph>Function Wizard</emph>, choose <link href="text/scalc/01/04060000.xhp" name="Insert - Function"><emph>Insert - Function</emph></link>.
<bookmarkvalue>ABS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>absolute values</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>values;absolute</bookmarkvalue>
ABS
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCABS">Returns the absolute value of a number.</ahelp>
ABS(Number)
<emph>Number</emph> is the number whose absolute value is to be calculated. The absolute value of a number is its value without the +/- sign.
<item type="input">=ABS(-56)</item> returns 56.
<item type="input">=ABS(12)</item> returns 12.
<item type="input">=ABS(0)</item> returns 0.
<bookmarkvalue>ACOS function</bookmarkvalue>
ACOS
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARCCOS">Returns the inverse trigonometric cosine of a number.</ahelp>
ACOS(Number)
This function returns the inverse trigonometric cosine of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the angle (in radians) whose cosine is Number. The angle returned is between 0 and PI.
To return the angle in degrees, use the DEGREES function.
<item type="input">=ACOS(-1)</item> returns 3.14159265358979 (PI radians)
<item type="input">=DEGREES(ACOS(0.5))</item> returns 60. The cosine of 60 degrees is 0.5.
<bookmarkvalue>ACOSH function</bookmarkvalue>
ACOSH
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARCOSHYP">Returns the inverse hyperbolic cosine of a number.</ahelp>
ACOSH(Number)
This function returns the inverse hyperbolic cosine of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the number whose hyperbolic cosine is Number.
Number must be greater than or equal to 1.
<item type="input">=ACOSH(1)</item> returns 0.
<item type="input">=ACOSH(COSH(4))</item> returns 4.
<bookmarkvalue>ACOT function</bookmarkvalue>
ACOT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARCCOT">Returns the inverse cotangent (the arccotangent) of the given number.</ahelp>
ACOT(Number)
This function returns the inverse trigonometric cotangent of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the angle (in radians) whose cotangent is Number. The angle returned is between 0 and PI.
<item type="input">=ACOT(1)</item> returns 0.785398163397448 (PI/4 radians).
<item type="input">=DEGREES(ACOT(1))</item> returns 45. The tangent of 45 degrees is 1.
<bookmarkvalue>ACOTH function</bookmarkvalue>
ACOTH
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARCOTHYP">Returns the inverse hyperbolic cotangent of the given number.</ahelp>
ACOTH(Number)
This function returns the inverse hyperbolic cotangent of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the number whose hyperbolic cotangent is Number.
An error results if Number is between -1 and 1 inclusive.
<item type="input">=ACOTH(1.1)</item> returns inverse hyperbolic cotangent of 1.1, approximately 1.52226.
<bookmarkvalue>ASIN function</bookmarkvalue>
ASIN
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARCSIN">Returns the inverse trigonometric sine of a number.</ahelp>
ASIN(Number)
This function returns the inverse trigonometric sine of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the angle (in radians) whose sine is Number. The angle returned is between -PI/2 and +PI/2.
<item type="input">=ASIN(0)</item> returns 0.
<item type="input">=ASIN(1)</item> returns 1.5707963267949 (PI/2 radians).
<item type="input">=DEGREES(ASIN(0.5))</item> returns 30. The sine of 30 degrees is 0.5.
<bookmarkvalue>ASINH function</bookmarkvalue>
ASINH
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARSINHYP">Returns the inverse hyperbolic sine of a number.</ahelp>
ASINH(Number)
This function returns the inverse hyperbolic sine of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the number whose hyperbolic sine is Number.
<item type="input">=ASINH(-90)</item> returns approximately -5.1929877.
<item type="input">=ASINH(SINH(4))</item> returns 4.
<bookmarkvalue>ATAN function</bookmarkvalue>
ATAN
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARCTAN">Returns the inverse trigonometric tangent of a number.</ahelp>
ATAN(Number)
This function returns the inverse trigonometric tangent of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the angle (in radians) whose tangent is Number. The angle returned is between -PI/2 and PI/2.
<item type="input">=ATAN(1)</item> returns 0.785398163397448 (PI/4 radians).
<item type="input">=DEGREES(ATAN(1))</item> returns 45. The tangent of 45 degrees is 1.
<bookmarkvalue>ATAN2 function</bookmarkvalue>
ATAN2
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARCTAN2">Returns the angle (in radians) between the x-axis and a line from the origin to the point (NumberX|NumberY).</ahelp>
ATAN2(NumberX; NumberY)
<emph>NumberX</emph> is the value of the x coordinate.
<emph>NumberY</emph> is the value of the y coordinate.
Programming languages have usually the opposite order of arguments for their atan2() function.
ATAN2 returns the angle (in radians) between the x-axis and a line from the origin to the point (NumberX|NumberY)
<item type="input">=ATAN2(-5;9)</item> returns 2.07789 radians.
To get the angle in degrees apply the DEGREES function to the result.
<input>=DEGREES(ATAN2(12.3;12.3))</input> returns 45. The tangent of 45 degrees is 1.
%PRODUCTNAME results 0 for ATAN2(0;0).
The function can be used in converting cartesian coordinates to polar coordinates.
=DEGREES(ATAN2(-8;5)) returns φ =  147.9 degrees
<image id="imgid3150758" src="media/helpimg/scalc/coordinates-to-polar-01.svg" width="2.5inch" height="1.5inch"><alt id="altid3150758">Cartesian coordinates to polar coordinates example</alt></image>
<bookmarkvalue>ATANH function</bookmarkvalue>
ATANH
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCARTANHYP">Returns the inverse hyperbolic tangent of a number.</ahelp>
ATANH(Number)
This function returns the inverse hyperbolic tangent of <emph>Number</emph>, that is the number whose hyperbolic tangent is Number.
Number must obey the condition -1 < number < 1.
<item type="input">=ATANH(0)</item> returns 0.
<bookmarkvalue>COS function</bookmarkvalue>
COS
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCOS">Returns the cosine of the given angle (in radians).</ahelp>
COS(Number)
Returns the (trigonometric) cosine of <emph>Number</emph>, the angle in radians.
To return the cosine of an angle in degrees, use the RADIANS function.
<item type="input">=COS(PI()*2)</item> returns 1, the cosine of 2*PI radians.
<item type="input">=COS(RADIANS(60))</item> returns 0.5, the cosine of 60 degrees.
<bookmarkvalue>COSH function</bookmarkvalue>
COSH
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCOSHYP">Returns the hyperbolic cosine of a number.</ahelp>
COSH(Number)
Returns the hyperbolic cosine of <emph>Number</emph>.
<item type="input">=COSH(0)</item> returns 1, the hyperbolic cosine of 0.
<bookmarkvalue>COT function</bookmarkvalue>
COT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCOT">Returns the cotangent of the given angle (in radians).</ahelp>
COT(Number)
Returns the (trigonometric) cotangent of <emph>Number</emph>, the angle in radians.
To return the cotangent of an angle in degrees, use the RADIANS function.
The cotangent of an angle is equivalent to 1 divided by the tangent of that angle.
Examples:
<item type="input">=COT(PI()/4)</item> returns 1, the cotangent of PI/4 radians.
<item type="input">=COT(RADIANS(45))</item> returns 1, the cotangent of 45 degrees.
<bookmarkvalue>COTH function</bookmarkvalue>
COTH
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCOTHYP">Returns the hyperbolic cotangent of a given number (angle).</ahelp>
COTH(Number)
Returns the hyperbolic cotangent of <emph>Number</emph>.
<item type="input">=COTH(1)</item> returns the hyperbolic cotangent of 1, approximately 1.3130.
<bookmarkvalue>CSC function</bookmarkvalue>
CSC
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCOSECANT">Returns the cosecant of the given angle (in radians). The cosecant of an angle is equivalent to 1 divided by the sine of that angle</ahelp>
CSC(Number)
Returns the (trigonometric) cosecant of <emph>Number</emph>, the angle in radians.
To return the cosecant of an angle in degrees, use the RADIANS function.
<item type="input">=CSC(PI()/4)</item> returns approximately 1.4142135624, the inverse of the sine of PI/4 radians.
<item type="input">=CSC(RADIANS(30))</item> returns 2, the cosecant of 30 degrees.
<bookmarkvalue>CSCH function</bookmarkvalue>
CSCH
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCOSECANTHYP">Returns the hyperbolic cosecant of a number.</ahelp>
CSCH(Number)
Returns the hyperbolic cosecant of <emph>Number</emph>.
<item type="input">=CSCH(1)</item> returns approximately 0.8509181282, the hyperbolic cosecant of 1.

<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCDEG">Converts radians into degrees.</ahelp>
DEGREES(Number)
<emph>Number</emph> is the angle in radians to be converted to degrees.
<item type="input">=DEGREES(PI())</item> returns 180 degrees.

FACT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCFAKULTAET">Returns the factorial of a number.</ahelp>
FACT(Number)
Returns Number!, the factorial of <emph>Number</emph>, calculated as 1*2*3*4* ... * Number.
=FACT(0) returns 1 by definition.
The factorial of a negative number returns the "invalid argument" error.
<item type="input">=FACT(3)</item> returns 6.
<item type="input">=FACT(0)</item> returns 1.

<bookmarkvalue>GCD function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>greatest common divisor</bookmarkvalue>
GCD
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCGGT">Returns the greatest common divisor of two or more integers.</ahelp>
The greatest common divisor is the positive largest integer which will divide, without remainder, each of the given integers.
<item type="input">=GCD(16;32;24) </item>gives the result 8, because 8 is the largest number that can divide 16, 24 and 32 without a remainder.
<item type="input">=GCD(B1:B3)</item> where cells B1, B2, B3 contain <item type="input">9</item>, <item type="input">12</item>, <item type="input">9</item> gives 3.

<bookmarkvalue>COMBIN function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>number of combinations</bookmarkvalue>
COMBIN
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCKOMBINATIONEN">Returns the number of combinations for elements without repetition.</ahelp>
COMBIN(Count1; Count2)
<emph>Count1</emph> is the number of items in the set.
<emph>Count2</emph> is the number of items to choose from the set.
COMBIN returns the number of ordered ways to choose these items. For example if there are 3 items A, B and C in a set, you can choose 2 items in 3 different ways, namely AB, AC and BC.
COMBIN implements the formula: Count1!/(Count2!*(Count1-Count2)!)
<item type="input">=COMBIN(3;2)</item> returns 3.
<bookmarkvalue>COMBINA function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>number of combinations with repetitions</bookmarkvalue>
COMBINA
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCKOMBINATIONEN2">Returns the number of combinations of a subset of items including repetitions.</ahelp>
COMBINA(Count1; Count2)
COMBINA returns the number of unique ways to choose these items, where the order of choosing is irrelevant, and repetition of items is allowed. For example if there are 3 items A, B and C in a set, you can choose 2 items in 6 different ways, namely AA, AB, AC, BB, BC and CC.
COMBINA implements the formula: (Count1+Count2-1)! / (Count2!(Count1-1)!)
<item type="input">=COMBINA(3;2)</item> returns 6.
<bookmarkvalue>TRUNC function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>decimal places;cutting off</bookmarkvalue>
TRUNC
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCKUERZEN">Truncates a number by removing decimal places.</ahelp>
TRUNC(Number; Count)
Returns <emph>Number</emph> with at most <emph>Count</emph> decimal places. Excess decimal places are simply removed, irrespective of sign.
<item type="literal">TRUNC(Number; 0)</item> behaves as <item type="literal">INT(Number)</item> for positive numbers, but effectively rounds towards zero for negative numbers.
The <emph>visible</emph> decimal places of the result are specified in <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC">%PRODUCTNAME - Preferences</caseinline><defaultinline>Tools - Options</defaultinline></switchinline> - <link href="text/shared/optionen/01060500.xhp">%PRODUCTNAME Calc - Calculate</link>.
<item type="input">=TRUNC(1.239;2)</item> returns 1.23. The 9 is lost.
<item type="input">=TRUNC(-1.234999;3)</item> returns -1.234. All the 9s are lost.

MULTINOMIAL
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCMULTINOMIAL">Returns the factorial of the sum of the arguments divided by the product of the factorials of the arguments.</ahelp>
<item type="input">=MULTINOMIAL(F11:H11)</item> returns 1260, if F11 to H11 contain the values <item type="input">2</item>, <item type="input">3</item> and <item type="input">4</item>. This corresponds to the formula =(2+3+4)! / (2!*3!*4!)

POWER
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCPOTENZ">Returns a number raised to another number.</ahelp>
POWER(Base; Exponent)
Returns <emph>Base</emph> raised to the power of <emph>Exponent</emph>.
The same result may be achieved by using the exponentiation operator ^:
<item type="literal">Base^Exponent</item>
<literal>=POWER(0,0)</literal> returns 1.
<item type="input">=POWER(4;3)</item> returns 64, which is 4 to the power of 3.
=4^3 also returns 4 to the power of 3.
<bookmarkvalue>SERIESSUM function</bookmarkvalue>
SERIESSUM
<ahelp hid=".">Sums the first terms of a power series.</ahelp>
SERIESSUM(x;n;m;c) = c<sub>1</sub>x<sup>n</sup> + c<sub>2</sub>x<sup>n+m</sup> + c<sub>3</sub>x<sup>n+2m</sup> + ... + c<sub>i</sub>x<sup>n + (i-1)m</sup>.
SERIESSUM(X; N; M; Coefficients)
<emph>X</emph> is the input value for the power series.
<emph>N</emph> is the initial power
<emph>M</emph> is the increment to increase N
<emph>Coefficients</emph> is a series of coefficients. For each coefficient the series sum is extended by one section.

<bookmarkvalue>MOD function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>remainders of divisions</bookmarkvalue>
MOD
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCREST">Returns the remainder when one integer is divided by another.</ahelp>
MOD(Dividend; Divisor)
For integer arguments this function returns Dividend modulo Divisor, that is the remainder when <emph>Dividend</emph> is divided by <emph>Divisor</emph>.
This function is implemented as <item type="literal">Dividend - Divisor * INT(Dividend/Divisor)</item> , and this formula gives the result if the arguments are not integer.
<item type="input">=MOD(22;3)</item> returns 1, the remainder when 22 is divided by 3.
<item type="input">=MOD(11.25;2.5)</item> returns 1.25.
<bookmarkvalue>QUOTIENT function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>divisions</bookmarkvalue>
QUOTIENT
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCQUOTIENT">Returns the integer part of a division operation.</ahelp>
QUOTIENT(Numerator; Denominator)
Returns the integer part of <emph>Numerator</emph> divided by <emph>Denominator</emph>.
QUOTIENT is equivalent to <item type="literal">INT(numerator/denominator)</item> for same-sign numerator and denominator, except that it may report errors with different error codes. More generally, it is equivalent to <item type="literal">INT(numerator/denominator/SIGN(numerator/denominator))*SIGN(numerator/denominator)</item>.
<item type="input">=QUOTIENT(11;3)</item> returns 3. The remainder of 2 is lost.

<bookmarkvalue>ROUND function</bookmarkvalue>
ROUND
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCRUNDEN">Rounds a number to a certain number of decimal places.</ahelp>
ROUND(Number [; Count])
Returns <emph>Number</emph> rounded to <emph>Count</emph> decimal places. If Count is omitted or zero, the function rounds to the nearest integer. If Count is negative, the function rounds to the nearest 10, 100, 1000, etc.
This function rounds to the nearest number. See ROUNDDOWN and ROUNDUP for alternatives.
<item type="input">=ROUND(2.348;2)</item> returns 2.35
<item type="input">=ROUND(-32.4834;3)</item> returns -32.483. Change the cell format to see all decimals.
<item type="input">=ROUND(2.348;0)</item> returns 2.
<item type="input">=ROUND(2.5)</item> returns 3.
<item type="input">=ROUND(987.65;-2)</item> returns 1000.
<bookmarkvalue>ROUNDDOWN function</bookmarkvalue>
ROUNDDOWN
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCABRUNDEN">Rounds a number down, toward zero, to a certain precision.</ahelp>
ROUNDDOWN(Number [; Count])
Returns <emph>Number</emph> rounded down (towards zero) to <emph>Count</emph> decimal places. If Count is omitted or zero, the function rounds down to an integer. If Count is negative, the function rounds down to the next 10, 100, 1000, etc.
This function rounds towards zero. See ROUNDUP and ROUND for alternatives.
<item type="input">=ROUNDDOWN(1.234;2)</item> returns 1.23.
<item type="input">=ROUNDDOWN(45.67;0)</item> returns 45.
<item type="input">=ROUNDDOWN(-45.67)</item> returns -45.
<item type="input">=ROUNDDOWN(987.65;-2)</item> returns 900.
<bookmarkvalue>ROUNDUP function</bookmarkvalue>
ROUNDUP
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCAUFRUNDEN">Rounds a number up, away from zero, to a certain precision.</ahelp>
ROUNDUP(Number [; Count])
Returns <emph>Number</emph> rounded up (away from zero) to <emph>Count</emph> decimal places. If Count is omitted or zero, the function rounds up to an integer. If Count is negative, the function rounds up to the next 10, 100, 1000, etc.
This function rounds away from zero. See ROUNDDOWN and ROUND for alternatives.
<item type="input">=ROUNDUP(1.1111;2)</item> returns 1.12.
<item type="input">=ROUNDUP(1.2345;1)</item> returns 1.3.
<item type="input">=ROUNDUP(45.67;0)</item> returns 46.
<item type="input">=ROUNDUP(-45.67)</item> returns -46.
<item type="input">=ROUNDUP(987.65;-2)</item> returns 1000.

<bookmarkvalue>SUM function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>adding;numbers in cell ranges</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="sumhead"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060106.xhp#Section16">SUM</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCSUMME">Adds a set of numbers.</ahelp>
SUM ignores any text or empty cell within a range or array. If you suspect wrong results of the SUM function, look for text in the data ranges. Use the <link href="text/scalc/01/03080000.xhp" name="value highlight">value highlighting</link> feature to highlight the text contents in the range that may represent a number.
If you enter the numbers <item type="input">2</item>; <item type="input">3 </item>and <item type="input">4</item> in the Number 1; 2 and 3 text boxes, 9 will be returned as the result.
<item type="input">=SUM(A1;A3;B5)</item> calculates the sum of the three cells. <item type="input">=SUM (A1:E10)</item> calculates the sum of all cells in the A1 to E10 cell range.
Conditions linked by AND can be used with the function SUM() in the following manner:
Example assumption: You have entered invoices into a table. Column A contains the date value of the invoice, column B the amounts. You want to find a formula that you can use to return the total of all amounts only for a specific month, e.g. only the amount for the period >=2008-01-01 to <2008-02-01. The range with the date values covers A1:A40, the range containing the amounts to be totaled is B1:B40. C1 contains the start date, 2008<item type="input">-01-01</item>, of the invoices to be included and C2 the date, 2008<item type="input">-02-01</item>, that is no longer included.
Enter the following formula as an array formula:
<item type="input">=SUM((A1:A40>=C1)*(A1:A40<C2)*B1:B40)</item>
In order to enter this as an array formula, you must press the Shift<switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC">+Command</caseinline><defaultinline>+ Ctrl</defaultinline></switchinline>+ Enter keys instead of simply pressing the Enter key to close the formula. The formula will then be shown in the <emph>Formula</emph> bar enclosed in braces.
{=SUM((A1:A40>=C1)*(A1:A40<C2)*B1:B40)}
The formula is based on the fact that the result of a comparison is 1 if the criterion is met and 0 if it is not met. The individual comparison results will be treated as an array and used in matrix multiplication, and at the end the individual values will be totaled to give the result matrix.
<bookmarkvalue>SUMIF function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>adding;specified numbers</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="sumifhead"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060106.xhp#Section15">SUMIF</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCSUMMEWENN">Adds the cells specified by a given criteria.</ahelp> This function is used to browse a range when you search for a certain value.
SUMIF(Range; Criteria [; SumRange])
<emph>Range</emph> is the range to which the criteria are to be applied.
<emph>Criteria</emph> is the cell in which the search criterion is shown, or the search criterion itself. If the criteria is written into the formula, it has to be surrounded by double quotes.
<emph>SumRange</emph> is the range from which values are summed. If this parameter has not been indicated, the values found in the Range are summed.
SUMIF supports the reference concatenation operator () only in the Criteria parameter, and only if the optional SumRange parameter is not given.
To sum up only negative numbers: <item type="input">=SUMIF(A1:A10;"<0")</item>
<item type="input">=SUMIF(A1:A10;">0";B1:B10)</item> - sums values from the range B1:B10 only if the corresponding values in the range A1:A10 are >0.
See COUNTIF() for some more syntax examples that can be used with SUMIF().

<bookmarkvalue>AutoFilter function; subtotals</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>sums;of filtered data</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>filtered data; sums</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>SUBTOTAL function</bookmarkvalue>
SUBTOTAL
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCTEILERGEBNIS">Calculates subtotals.</ahelp> If a range already contains subtotals, these are not used for further calculations. Use this function with the AutoFilters to take only the filtered records into account.
SUBTOTAL(Function; Range)
<emph>Function</emph> is a number that stands for one of the following functions:
Function index
(includes hidden values)
(ignores hidden values)
AVERAGE
COUNT
COUNTA
MAX
MIN
STDEV
STDEVP
SUM
VAR
VARP
Use numbers 1-11 to include manually hidden rows or 101-111 to exclude them; filtered-out cells are always excluded.
<emph>Range</emph> is the range whose cells are included.
You have a table in the cell range A1:B6 containing a bill of material for 10 students. Row 2 (Pen) is manually hidden. You want to see the sum of the figures that are displayed; that is, just the subtotal for the filtered rows. In this case the correct formula would be:
<emph>ITEM</emph>
<emph>QUANTITY</emph>
Pen
Pencil
Notebook
Rubber
Sharpener
<item type="input">=SUBTOTAL(9;B2:B6) returns 50.</item>
<item type="input">=SUBTOTAL(109;B2:B6) returns 40.</item>
<bookmarkvalue>Euro; converting</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>EUROCONVERT function</bookmarkvalue>
EUROCONVERT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCUMRECHNEN">Converts between old European national currency and to and from Euros.</ahelp>
EUROCONVERT(Value; "Fromcurrency"; "Tocurrency" [; fullprecision [; triangulationprecision]])
<emph>Value</emph> is the amount of the currency to be converted.
<emph>Fromcurrency</emph> and <emph>Tocurrency</emph> are the currency units to convert from and to respectively. These must be text, the official abbreviation for the currency (for example, "EUR"). The rates (shown per Euro) were set by the European Commission.
<emph>Fullprecision</emph> is optional. If omitted or False, the result is rounded according to the decimals of the To currency. If Fullprecision is True, the result is not rounded.
<emph>Triangulationprecision</emph> is optional. If Triangulationprecision is given and >=3, the intermediate result of a triangular conversion (currency1,EUR,currency2) is rounded to that precision. If Triangulationprecision is omitted, the intermediate result is not rounded. Also if To currency is "EUR", Triangulationprecision is used as if triangulation was needed and conversion from EUR to EUR was applied.
<emph>Examples</emph>
<item type="input">=EUROCONVERT(100;"ATS";"EUR")</item> converts 100 Austrian Schillings into Euros.
<item type="input">=EUROCONVERT(100;"EUR";"DEM")</item> converts 100 Euros into German Marks.
<bookmarkvalue>CONVERTOOO function</bookmarkvalue>
CONVERTOOO
<ahelp hid=".">Converts a value from one unit of measurement to another unit of measurement. The conversion factors are given in a list in the configuration.</ahelp>
At one time the list of conversion factors included the legacy European currencies and the Euro (see examples below). We suggest using the new function EUROCONVERT for converting these currencies.
CONVERTOOO(value; "text"; "text")
<item type="input">=CONVERTOOO(100;"ATS";"EUR")</item> returns the Euro value of 100 Austrian Schillings.
=CONVERTOOO(100;"EUR";"DEM") converts 100 Euros into German Marks.

<bookmarkvalue>MROUND function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>nearest multiple</bookmarkvalue>
MROUND
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCMROUND">Returns a number rounded to the nearest multiple of another number.</ahelp>
MROUND(Number; Multiple)
Returns <emph>Number</emph> rounded to the nearest multiple of <emph>Multiple</emph>.
An alternative implementation would be <item type="literal">Multiple * ROUND(Number/Multiple)</item>.
<item type="input">=MROUND(15.5;3)</item> returns 15, as 15.5 is closer to 15 (= 3*5) than to 18 (= 3*6).
<item type="input">=MROUND(1.4;0.5)</item> returns 1.5 (= 0.5*3).
<bookmarkvalue>SQRT function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>square roots;positive numbers</bookmarkvalue>
SQRT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCWURZEL">Returns the positive square root of a number.</ahelp>
SQRT(Number)
Returns the positive square root of <emph>Number</emph>.
Number must be positive.
<item type="input">=SQRT(16)</item> returns 4.
<item type="input">=SQRT(-16)</item> returns an <item type="literal">invalid argument</item> error.
<bookmarkvalue>SQRTPI function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>square roots;products of Pi</bookmarkvalue>
SQRTPI
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCSQRTPI">Returns the square root of (PI times a number).</ahelp>
SQRTPI(Number)
Returns the positive square root of (PI multiplied by <emph>Number</emph>).
This is equivalent to <item type="literal">SQRT(PI()*Number)</item>.
<item type="input">=SQRTPI(2)</item> returns the squareroot of (2PI), approximately 2.506628.
<bookmarkvalue>random numbers; between limits</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>RANDBETWEEN function</bookmarkvalue>
RANDBETWEEN
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCRANDBETWEEN">Returns an integer random number in a specified range.</ahelp>
RANDBETWEEN(Bottom; Top)
Returns an integer random number between integers <emph>Bottom</emph> and <emph>Top</emph> (both inclusive).
This function produces a new random number each time Calc recalculates. To force Calc to recalculate manually press F9.
To generate random numbers which never recalculate, copy cells containing this function, and use <item type="menuitem">Edit - Paste Special</item> (with <item type="menuitem">Paste All</item> and <item type="menuitem">Formulas</item> not marked and <item type="menuitem">Numbers</item> marked).
<item type="input">=RANDBETWEEN(20;30)</item> returns an integer of between 20 and 30.
<bookmarkvalue>random numbers non-volatile; between limits</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>RANDBETWEEN.NV function</bookmarkvalue>
RANDBETWEEN.NV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCRANDBETWEENNV">Returns an non-volatile integer random number in a specified range.</ahelp>
RANDBETWEEN.NV(Bottom; Top)
Returns an non-volatile integer random number between integers <emph>Bottom</emph> and <emph>Top</emph> (both inclusive). A non-volatile function is not recalculated at new input events or pressing <keycode>F9</keycode>. However, the function is recalculated when pressing <keycode>F9</keycode> with the cursor on the cell containing the function, when opening the file, and when <emph>Top</emph> or <emph>Bottom</emph> are recalculated.
<input>=RANDBETWEEN.NV(20;30)</input> returns a non-volatile integer between 20 and 30.
<input>=RANDBETWEEN.NV(A1;30)</input> returns a non-volatile integer between the value of cell A1 and 30. The function is recalculated when the contents of cell A1 change.
<bookmarkvalue>RAND function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>random numbers;between 0 and 1</bookmarkvalue>
RAND
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZUFALLSZAHL">Returns a random number between 0 and 1.</ahelp>
RAND()
To generate random numbers which never recalculate, either:
Copy cells each containing =RAND(), and use <menuitem>Edit - Paste Special</menuitem> (with <emph>Paste All</emph> and <emph>Formulas</emph> not marked and <emph>Numbers</emph> marked).
Use the Fill Cell command with random numbers (<menuitem>Sheet - Fill Cells - Fill Random Numbers</menuitem>).
Use the RAND.NV() function for non-volatile random numbers.
<item type="input">=RAND()</item> returns a random number between 0 and 1.
<bookmarkvalue>random numbers non-volatile;between 0 and 1</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>RAND.NV function</bookmarkvalue>
RAND.NV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCRANDNV">Returns a non-volatile random number between 0 and 1.</ahelp>
RAND.NV()
This function produces a non-volatile random number on input. A non-volatile function is not recalculated at new input events. The function does not recalculate when pressing <keycode>F9</keycode>, except when the cursor is on the cell containing the function. The function is recalculated when opening the file.
<input>=RAND.NV()</input> returns a non-volatile random number between 0 and 1.
Array Functions
<bookmarkvalue>matrices; functions</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>Function Wizard; arrays</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>array formulas</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>inline array constants</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>formulas; arrays</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>functions; array functions</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>editing; array formulas</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>copying; array formulas</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>adjusting array ranges</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>calculating; conditional calculations</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>matrices; calculations</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>conditional calculations with arrays</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>implicit array handling</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>forced array handling</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="arrayfunctit"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060107.xhp" name="array functions">Array Functions</link></variable>
<variable id="matrixtext">This category contains the array functions.</variable>
What is an Array?
<variable id="wasmatrix">An array is a linked range of cells on a spreadsheet containing values.</variable> A square range of 3 rows and 3 columns is a 3 x 3 array:
The smallest possible array is a 1 x 2 or 2 x 1 array with two adjacent cells.
What is an array formula?
A formula in which the individual values in a cell range are evaluated is referred to as an array formula. The difference between an array formula and other formulas is that the array formula deals with several values simultaneously instead of just one.
Not only can an array formula process several values, but it can also return several values. The results of an array formula is also an array.
To multiply the values in the individual cells by 10 in the above array, you do not need to apply a formula to each individual cell or value. Instead you just need to use a single array formula. Select a range of 3 x 3 cells on another part of the spreadsheet, enter the formula <item type="input">=10*A1:C3</item> and confirm this entry using the key combination <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + Shift + Enter</emph>. The result is a 3 x 3 array in which the individual values in the cell range (A1:C3) are multiplied by a factor of 10.
In addition to multiplication, you can also use other operators on the reference range (an array). With $[officename] Calc, you can add (+), subtract (-), multiply (*), divide (/), use exponents (^), concatenation () and comparisons (=, <>, <, >, <=, >=). The operators can be used on each individual value in the cell range and return the result as an array if the array formula was entered.
Comparison operators in an array formula treat empty cells in the same way as in a normal formula, that is, either as zero or as an empty string. For example, if cells A1 and A2 are empty the array formulas <item type="input">{=A1:A2=""}</item> and <item type="input">{=A1:A2=0}</item> will both return a 1 column 2 row array of cells containing TRUE.
When do you use array formulas?
Use array formulas if you have to repeat calculations using different values. If you decide to change the calculation method later, you only have to update the array formula. To add an array formula, select the entire array range and then <link href="text/scalc/01/04060107.xhp" name="make the required change to the array formula">make the required change to the array formula</link>.
Array formulas are also a space saving option when several values must be calculated, since they are not very memory-intensive. In addition, arrays are an essential tool for carrying out complex calculations, because you can have several cell ranges included in your calculations. $[officename] has different math functions for arrays, such as the MMULT function for multiplying two arrays or the SUMPRODUCT function for calculating the scalar products of two arrays.
Using Array Formulas in $[officename] Calc
You can also create a "normal" formula in which the reference range, such as parameters, indicate an array formula. The result is obtained from the intersection of the reference range and the rows or columns in which the formula is found. If there is no intersection or if the range at the intersection covers several rows or columns, a #VALUE! error message appears. The following example illustrates this concept:
Creating Array Formulas
If you create an array formula using the <emph>Function Wizard</emph>, you must mark the <emph>Array</emph> check box each time so that the results are returned in an array. Otherwise, only the value in the upper-left cell of the array being calculated is returned.
If you enter the array formula directly into the cell, you must use the key combination <emph>Shift + </emph><switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + Enter</emph> instead of the <emph>Enter</emph> key. Only then does the formula become an array formula.
Array formulas appear in braces in $[officename] Calc. You cannot create array formulas by manually entering the braces.
The cells in a results array are automatically protected against changes. However, you can edit or copy the array formula by selecting the entire array cell range.
Using Inline Array Constants in Formulas
Calc supports inline matrix/array constants in formulas. An inline array is surrounded by curly braces '{' and '}'. Elements can be each a number (including negatives), a logical constant (TRUE, FALSE), or a literal string. Non-constant expressions are not allowed. Arrays can be entered with one or more rows, and one or more columns. All rows must consist of the same number of elements, all columns must consist of the same number of elements.
The column separator (separating elements in one row) and the row separator are language and locale dependent. But in this help content, the ';' semicolon and '|' pipe symbol are used to indicate the column and row separators, respectively. For example, in the English locale, the ',' comma is used as the column separator, while the ';' semicolon is used as the row separator.
You can view and change the row and column separator in <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>%PRODUCTNAME - Preferences</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Tools - Options</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> - Calc - Formula - Separators</emph>.
Arrays can not be nested.
<emph>Examples:</emph>
={1;2;3}
An array with one row consisting of the three numbers 1, 2, and 3.
To enter this array constant, you select three cells in a row, then you type the formula <item type="input">={1;2;3}</item> using the curly braces and the semicolons, then press <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + Shift + Enter</emph>.
={1;2;3|4;5;6}
An array with two rows and three values in each row.
={0;1;2|FALSE;TRUE;"two"}
A mixed data array.
=SIN({1;2;3})
Entered as a matrix formula, delivers the result of three SIN calculations with the arguments 1, 2, and 3.
Editing Array Formulas
Select the cell range or array containing the array formula. To select the whole array, position the cell cursor inside the array range, then press <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + /</emph>, where <emph>/</emph> is the <emph>Division</emph> key on the numeric keypad.
Either press <emph>F2</emph> or position the cursor in the input line. Both of these actions let you edit the formula.
After you have made changes, press <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + Shift + Enter</emph>.
You can format the separate parts of an array. For example, you can change the font color. Select a cell range and then change the attribute you want.
Copying Array Formulas
Select the cell range or array containing the array formula.
Either press <emph>F2</emph> or position the cursor in the input line.
Copy the formula into the input line by pressing <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + C</emph>.
Select a range of cells where you want to insert the array formula and either press <emph>F2</emph> or position the cursor in the input line.
Paste the formula by pressing <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + V</emph> in the selected space and confirm it by pressing <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline><emph> + Shift + Enter</emph>. The selected range now contains the array formula.
Adjusting an Array Range
If you want to edit the output array, do the following:
Below the selection, to the right, you will see a small icon with which you can zoom in or out on the range using your mouse.
When you adjust the array range, the array formula will not automatically be adjusted. You are only changing the range in which the result will appear.
By holding down the <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><emph>Command</emph></caseinline><defaultinline><emph>Ctrl</emph></defaultinline></switchinline> key, you can create a copy of the array formula in the given range.
Conditional Array Calculations
A conditional array calculation is an array or matrix formula that includes an IF() or CHOOSE() function. The condition argument in the formula is an area reference or a matrix result.
In the following example, the >0 test of the {=IF(A1:A3>0;"yes";"no")} formula is applied to each cell in the range A1:A3 and the result is copied to the corresponding cell.
B (formula)
B (result)
{=IF(A1:A3>0;"yes";"no")}
yes
no
The following functions provide forced array handling: CORREL, COVAR, FORECAST, FTEST, INTERCEPT, MDETERM, MINVERSE, MMULT, MODE, PEARSON, PROB, RSQ, SLOPE, STEYX, SUMPRODUCT, SUMX2MY2, SUMX2PY2, SUMXMY2, TTEST. If you use area references as arguments when you call one of these functions, the functions behave as array functions. The following table provides an example of forced array handling:
C (forced array formula)
C (result)
=SUMPRODUCT(A1:A2+1)
#VALUE!
<bookmarkvalue>MUNIT function</bookmarkvalue>
MUNIT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCEINHEITSMATRIX">Returns the unitary square array of a certain size.</ahelp> The unitary array is a square array where the main diagonal elements equal 1 and all other array elements are equal to 0.
MUNIT(Dimensions)
<emph>Dimensions</emph> refers to the size of the array unit.
You can find a general introduction to Array functions at the top of this page.
Select a square range within the spreadsheet, for example, from A1 to E5.
Without deselecting the range, select the MUNIT function. Mark the <emph>Array</emph> check box. Enter the desired dimensions for the array unit, in this case <item type="input">5</item>, and click <emph>OK</emph>.
You can also enter the <item type="input">=MUNIT(5)</item> formula in the last cell of the selected range (E5), and press <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><item type="keycode">Shift + Command + Enter</item></caseinline><defaultinline><item type="keycode">Shift + Ctrl + Enter</item></defaultinline></switchinline>.
You now see a unit array with a range of A1:E5.
<bookmarkvalue>FREQUENCY function</bookmarkvalue>
FREQUENCY
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCHAEUFIGKEIT">Indicates the frequency distribution in a one-column-array.</ahelp> The function counts the number of values in the <emph>Data</emph> array that are within the values given by the <emph>Classes</emph> array.
FREQUENCY(Data; Classes)
<emph>Data</emph> represents the reference to the values to be counted.
<emph>Classes</emph> represents the array of the limit values.
In the following table, column A lists unsorted measurement values. Column B contains the upper limit you entered for the classes into which you want to divide the data in column A. According to the limit entered in B1, the FREQUENCY function returns the number of measured values less than or equal to 5. As the limit in B2 is 10, the FREQUENCY function returns the second result as the number of measured values that are greater than 5 and less than or equal to 10. The text you entered in B6, ">25", is only for reference purposes.
Select a single column range in which to enter the frequency according to the class limits. You must select one field more than the class ceiling. In this example, select the range C1:C6. Call up the FREQUENCY function in the <emph>Function Wizard</emph>. Select the <emph>Data</emph> range in (A1:A11), and then the <emph>Classes</emph> range in which you entered the class limits (B1:B6). Select the <emph>Array</emph> check box and click <emph>OK</emph>. You will see the frequency count in the range C1:C6.

MDETERM(Array)
