Add-in for Programming in $[officename] Calc
<bookmarkvalue>programming; add-ins</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>shared libraries; programming</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>external DLL functions</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>functions; $[officename] Calc add-in DLL</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>add-ins; for programming</bookmarkvalue>
The method of extending Calc by Add-Ins that is described in the following is outdated. The interfaces are still valid and supported, to ensure compatibility with existing Add-Ins, but for programming new Add-Ins you should use the new <link href="text/shared/guide/integratinguno.xhp" name="API functions">API functions</link>.
$[officename] Calc can be expanded by Add-Ins, which are external programming modules providing additional functions for working with spreadsheets. These are listed in the <emph>Function Wizard</emph> in the <emph>Add-In</emph> category. If you would like to program an Add-In yourself, you can learn here which functions must be exported by the <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">shared library</caseinline><defaultinline>external DLL</defaultinline></switchinline> so that the Add-In can be successfully attached.
$[officename] searches the Add-in folder defined in the configuration for a suitable <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">shared library</caseinline><defaultinline>DLL</defaultinline></switchinline>. To be recognized by $[officename], the <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">shared library</caseinline><defaultinline>DLL</defaultinline></switchinline> must have certain properties, as explained in the following. This information allows you to program your own Add-In for <emph>Function Wizard</emph> of $[officename] Calc.
The Add-In Concept
Each Add-In library provides several functions. Some functions are used for administrative purposes. You can choose almost any name for your own functions. However, they must also follow certain rules regarding parameter passing. The exact naming and calling conventions vary for different platforms.
Functions of <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">Shared Library</caseinline><defaultinline>AddIn DLL</defaultinline></switchinline>
At a minimum, the administrative functions <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="GetFunctionCount">GetFunctionCount</link> and <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="GetFunctionData">GetFunctionData</link> must exist. Using these, the functions as well as parameter types and return values can be determined. As return values, the Double and String types are supported. As parameters, additionally the cell areas <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="Double Array">Double Array</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="String Array">String Array</link>, and <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="Cell Array">Cell Array</link> are supported.
Parameters are passed using references. Therefore, a change of these values is basically possible. However, this is not supported in $[officename] Calc because it does not make sense within spreadsheets.
Libraries can be reloaded during runtime and their contents can be analyzed by the administrative functions. For each function, information is available about count and type of parameters, internal and external function names and an administrative number.
The functions are called synchronously and return their results immediately. Real time functions (asynchronous functions) are also possible; however, they are not explained in detail because of their complexity.
General information about the interface
The maximum number of parameters in an Add-In function attached to $[officename] Calc is 16: one return value and a maximum of 15 function input parameters.
The data types are defined as follows:
<emph>Data types</emph>
<emph>Definition</emph>
Under Windows: FAR PASCAL (far pascal)
Other: default (operating system specific default)
2 Byte unsigned Integer
8 byte platform-dependent format
Platform-dependent like int
PTRDOUBLE =0 pointer to a double
PTRSTRING =1 pointer to a zero-terminated string
PTRDOUBLEARR =2 pointer to a double array
PTRSTRINGARR =3 pointer to a string array
PTRCELLARR =4 pointer to a cell array
NONE =5
<switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">Shared Library</caseinline><defaultinline>DLL</defaultinline></switchinline> functions
Following you will find a description of those functions, which are called at the <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">Shared Library</caseinline><defaultinline>external DLL</defaultinline></switchinline>.
For all <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">Shared Library</caseinline><defaultinline>DLL</defaultinline></switchinline> functions, the following applies:
<emph>Output</emph>: Resulting value
<emph>Input</emph>: Any number of types (double, char*, double*, char**, Cell area), where the <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="Cell area">Cell area</link> is an array of types double array, string array, or cell array.
Returns the number of functions without the management functions of the reference parameter. Each function has a unique number between 0 and nCount-1. This number will be needed for the <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="GetFunctionData">GetFunctionData</link> and <link href="text/scalc/01/04060112.xhp" name="GetParameterDescription">GetParameterDescription</link> functions later.
<emph>Syntax</emph>
<emph>Parameter</emph>
<emph>Output</emph>: Reference to a variable, which is supposed to contain the number of Add-In functions. For example: If the Add-In provides 5 functions for $[officename] Calc, then nCount=5.
Determines all the important information about an Add-In function.
<emph>Input</emph>: Function number between 0 and nCount-1, inclusively.
<emph>Output</emph>: Function name as seen by the programmer, as it is named in the <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="UNIX">Shared Library</caseinline><defaultinline>DLL</defaultinline></switchinline>. This name does not determine the name used in the <emph>Function Wizard</emph>.
<emph>Output</emph>: Number of parameters in AddIn function. This number must be greater than 0, because there is always a result value; the maximum value is 16.
<emph>Output</emph>: Pointer to an array of exactly 16 variables of type Paramtype. The first nParamCount entries are filled with the suitable type of parameter.
<emph>Output</emph>: Function name as seen by the user, as it appears in the <emph>Function Wizard</emph>. May contain umlauts.
The pFuncName and pInternalName parameters are char arrays, which are implemented with size 256 in $[officename] Calc.
Provides a brief description of the Add-In function and its parameters. As an option, this function can be used to show a function and parameter description in the <emph>Function Wizard</emph>.
<literal>void CALLTYPE GetParameterDescription(USHORT nNo, USHORT nParam, char* pName, char* pDesc)</literal>
<emph>Input</emph>: Number of the function in the library; between 0 and nCount-1.
<emph>Input</emph>: Indicates, for which parameter the description is provided; parameters start at 1. If nParam is 0, the description itself is supposed to be provided in pDesc; in this case, pName does not have any meaning.
<emph>Output</emph>: Takes up the parameter name or type, for example, the word "Number" or "String" or "Date", and so on. Implemented in $[officename] Calc as char[256].
<emph>Output</emph>: Takes up the description of the parameter, for example, "Value, at which the universe is to be calculated." Implemented in $[officename] Calc as char[256].
pName and pDesc are char arrays; implemented in $[officename] Calc with size 256. Please note that the space available in the <emph>Function Wizard</emph> is limited and that the 256 characters cannot be fully used.
Cell areas
The following tables contain information about which data structures must be provided by an external program module in order to pass cell areas. $[officename] Calc distinguishes between three different arrays, depending on the data type.
Double Array
As a parameter, a cell area with values of the Number/Double type can be passed. A double array in $[officename] Calc is defined as follows:
Offset
Description
Col1
Column number in the upper-left corner of the cell area. Numbering starts at 0.
Row1
Row number in the upper-left corner of the cell area; numbering starts at 0.
Tab1
Table number in the upper-left corner of the cell area; numbering starts at 0.
Col2
Column number in the lower-right corner of the cell area. Numbering starts at 0.
Row2
Row number in the lower-right corner of the cell area; numbering starts at 0.
Tab2
Table number in the lower-right corner of the cell area; numbering starts at 0.
Count
Number of the following elements. Empty cells are not counted or passed.
Col
Column number of the element. Numbering starts at 0.
Row number of the element; numbering starts at 0.
Tab
Table number of the element; numbering starts at 0.
Error
Error number, where the value 0 is defined as "no error." If the element comes from a formula cell the error value is determined by the formula.
Value
8 byte IEEE variable of type double/floating point
Next element
String Array
A cell area, which contains values of data type Text and is passed as a string array. A string array in $[officename] Calc is defined as follows:
Len
Length of the following string, including closing zero byte. If the length including closing zero byte equals an odd value a second zero byte is added to the string so that an even value is achieved. Therefore, Len is calculated using ((StrLen+2)1).
String
String with closing zero byte
Cell Array
Cell arrays are used to call cell areas containing text as well as numbers. A cell array in $[officename] Calc is defined as follows:
Type
Type of cell content, 0 == Double, 1 == String
Value or Len
If type == 0: 8 byte IEEE variable of type double/floating point
If type == 1: Length of the following string, including closing zero byte. If the length including closing zero byte equals an odd value a second zero byte is added to the string so that an even value is achieved. Therefore, Len is calculated using ((StrLen+2)1).
26 if type==1
If type == 1: String with closing zero byte
32 or 26+Len
...
Add-in Functions, List of Analysis Functions Part One
<bookmarkvalue>add-ins; analysis functions</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>analysis functions</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="headaddinanalysisone"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060115.xhp" name="Add-in Functions, List of Analysis Functions Part One">Add-in Functions, List of Analysis Functions Part One</link></variable>
The Add-in functions are supplied by the <link href="text/sbasic/shared/calcfunctions.xhp" name="addinanalysis">UNO <literal>com.sun.star.sheet.addin.Analysis</literal> service</link>.
<bookmarkvalue>Bessel functions</bookmarkvalue>
BESSELI
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCBESSELI">Calculates the modified Bessel function of the first kind In(x).</ahelp>
BESSELI(X; N)
<emph>X</emph> is the value on which the function will be calculated.
<emph>N</emph> is a positive integer (N >= 0) representing the order of the Bessel function In(x)
=BESSELI(3.45, 4), returns 0.651416873060081
=BESSELI(3.45, 4.333), returns 0.651416873060081, same as above because the fractional part of N is ignored.
=BESSELI(-1, 3), returns -0.022168424924332
BESSELJ
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCBESSELJ">Calculates the Bessel function of the first kind Jn(x) (cylinder function).</ahelp>
BESSELJ(X; N)
<emph>N</emph> is a positive integer (N >= 0) representing the order of the Bessel function Jn(x)
=BESSELJ(3.45, 4), returns 0.196772639864984
=BESSELJ(3.45, 4.333), returns 0.196772639864984, same as above because the fractional part of N is ignored.
=BESSELJ(-1, 3), returns -0.019563353982668
BESSELK
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCBESSELK">Calculates the modified Bessel function of the second kind Kn(x).</ahelp>
BESSELK(X; N)
<emph>X</emph> is the strictly positive value (X > 0) on which the function will be calculated.
<emph>N</emph> is a positive integer (N >= 0) representing the order of the Bessel function Kn(x)
=BESSELK(3.45, 4), returns 0.144803466373734
=BESSELK(3.45, 4.333), returns 0.144803466373734, same as above because the fractional part of N is ignored.
=BESSELK(0, 3), returns Err:502 – invalid argument (X=0)
BESSELY
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCBESSELY">Calculates the Bessel function of the second kind Yn(x).</ahelp>
BESSELY(X; N)
<emph>N</emph> is a positive integer (N >= 0) representing the order of the Bessel function Yn(x)
=BESSELY(3.45, 4), returns -0.679848116844476
=BESSELY(3.45, 4.333), returns -0.679848116844476, same as above because the fractional part of N is ignored.
=BESSELY(0, 3), returns Err:502 – invalid argument (X=0)
<bookmarkvalue>BIN2DEC function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;binary numbers, into decimal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
BIN2DEC
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCBIN2DEC">The result is the decimal number for the binary number entered.</ahelp>
BIN2DEC(Number)
<emph>Number</emph> is a binary number. The number can have a maximum of 10 places (bits). The most significant bit is the sign bit. Negative numbers are entered as two's complement.
<item type="input">=BIN2DEC(1100100)</item> returns 100.
<bookmarkvalue>BIN2HEX function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;binary numbers, into hexadecimal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
BIN2HEX
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCBIN2HEX">The result is the hexadecimal number for the binary number entered.</ahelp>
BIN2HEX(Number [; Places])
Places means the number of places to be output.
<item type="input">=BIN2HEX(1100100;6)</item> returns 000064.
<bookmarkvalue>BIN2OCT function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;binary numbers, into octal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
BIN2OCT
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCBIN2OCT"> The result is the octal number for the binary number entered.</ahelp>
BIN2OCT(Number [; Places])
<emph>Places</emph> means the number of places to be output.
<item type="input">=BIN2OCT(1100100;4)</item> returns 0144.
<bookmarkvalue>DELTA function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>recognizing;equal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
DELTA
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCDELTA">The result is TRUE (1) if both numbers, which are delivered as an argument, are equal, otherwise it is FALSE (0).</ahelp>
DELTA(Number1 [; Number2])
<item type="input">=DELTA(1;2)</item> returns 0.
<bookmarkvalue>DEC2BIN function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;decimal numbers, into binary numbers</bookmarkvalue>
DEC2BIN
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCDEC2BIN"> The result is the binary number for the decimal number entered between -512 and 511.</ahelp>
DEC2BIN(Number [; Places])
<emph>Number</emph> is a decimal number. If Number is negative, the function returns a binary number with 10 characters. The most significant bit is the sign bit, the other 9 bits return the value.
<item type="input">=DEC2BIN(100;8)</item> returns 01100100.
<bookmarkvalue>DEC2HEX function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;decimal numbers, into hexadecimal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
DEC2HEX
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCDEC2HEX">The result is the hexadecimal number for the decimal number entered.</ahelp>
DEC2HEX(Number [; Places])
<emph>Number</emph> is a decimal number. If Number is negative, the function returns a hexadecimal number with 10 characters (40 bits). The most significant bit is the sign bit, the other 39 bits return the value.
<item type="input">=DEC2HEX(100;4)</item> returns 0064.
<bookmarkvalue>DEC2OCT function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;decimal numbers, into octal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
DEC2OCT
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCDEC2OCT">The result is the octal number for the decimal number entered.</ahelp>
DEC2OCT(Number [; Places])
<emph>Number</emph> is a decimal number. If Number is negative, the function returns an octal number with 10 characters (30 bits). The most significant bit is the sign bit, the other 29 bits return the value.
<item type="input">=DEC2OCT(100;4)</item> returns 0144.
<bookmarkvalue>ERF function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>Gaussian error integral</bookmarkvalue>
ERF
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCERF">Returns values of the Gaussian error integral.</ahelp>
ERF(LowerLimit [; UpperLimit])
<emph>LowerLimit</emph> is the lower limit of the integral.
<emph>UpperLimit</emph> is optional. It is the upper limit of the integral. If this value is missing, the calculation takes place between 0 and the lower limit.
<item type="input">=ERF(0;1)</item> returns 0.842701.
<bookmarkvalue>ERF.PRECISE function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>Gaussian error integral</bookmarkvalue>
ERF.PRECISE
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCERFMS">Returns values of the Gaussian error integral between 0 and the given limit.</ahelp>
ERF.PRECISE(LowerLimit)
<emph>LowerLimit</emph> is the limit of the integral. The calculation takes place between 0 and this limit.
<item type="input">=ERF.PRECISE(1)</item> returns 0.842701.
<bookmarkvalue>ERFC function</bookmarkvalue>
ERFC
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCERFC">Returns complementary values of the Gaussian error integral between x and infinity.</ahelp>
ERFC(LowerLimit)
<emph>LowerLimit</emph> is the lower limit of the integral
<item type="input">=ERFC(1)</item> returns 0.157299.
<bookmarkvalue>ERFC.PRECISE function</bookmarkvalue>
ERFC.PRECISE
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCERFCMS">Returns complementary values of the Gaussian error integral between x and infinity.</ahelp>
ERFC.PRECISE(LowerLimit)
<item type="input">=ERFC.PRECISE(1)</item> returns 0.157299.
<bookmarkvalue>GESTEP function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>numbers;greater than or equal to</bookmarkvalue>
GESTEP
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCGESTEP">The result is 1 if <item type="literal">Number</item> is greater than or equal to <item type="literal">Step</item>.</ahelp>
GESTEP(Number [; Step])
<item type="input">=GESTEP(5;1)</item> returns 1.
<bookmarkvalue>HEX2BIN function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;hexadecimal numbers, into binary numbers</bookmarkvalue>
HEX2BIN
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCHEX2BIN">The result is the binary number for the hexadecimal number entered.</ahelp>
HEX2BIN(Number [; Places])
<emph>Number</emph> is a hexadecimal number or a string that represents a hexadecimal number. It can have a maximum of 10 places. The most significant bit is the sign bit, the following bits return the value. Negative numbers are entered as two's complement.
<emph>Places</emph> is the number of places to be output.
<item type="input">=HEX2BIN("6a";8)</item> returns 01101010.
<bookmarkvalue>HEX2DEC function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>converting;hexadecimal numbers, into decimal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
HEX2DEC
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCHEX2DEC">The result is the decimal number for the hexadecimal number entered.</ahelp>
HEX2DEC(Number)
<item type="input">=HEX2DEC("6a")</item> returns 106.

HEX2OCT

HEX2OCT(Number [; Places])
<item type="input">=HEX2OCT("6a";4)</item> returns 0152.

<bookmarkvalue>IMDIV function</bookmarkvalue>
IMDIV
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMDIV">The result is the division of two complex numbers.</ahelp>
IMDIV("Numerator"; "Denominator")
<emph>Numerator</emph>, <emph>Denominator</emph> are complex numbers that are entered in the form "x+yi" or "x+yj".
<item type="input">=IMDIV("-238+240i";"10+24i")</item> returns 5+12i.
<bookmarkvalue>IMEXP function</bookmarkvalue>
IMEXP
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMEXP">The result is the power of e and the complex number.</ahelp> The constant e has a value of approximately 2.71828182845904.
IMEXP("ComplexNumber")
<item type="input">=IMEXP("1+j") </item>returns 1.47+2.29j (rounded).
<bookmarkvalue>IMCONJUGATE function</bookmarkvalue>
IMCONJUGATE
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMCONJUGATE">The result is the conjugated complex complement to a complex number.</ahelp>
IMCONJUGATE("ComplexNumber")
<item type="input">=IMCONJUGATE("1+j")</item> returns 1-j.
<bookmarkvalue>IMLN function</bookmarkvalue>
IMLN
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMLN">The result is the natural logarithm (to the base e) of a complex number.</ahelp> The constant e has a value of approximately 2.71828182845904.
IMLN("ComplexNumber")
<item type="input">=IMLN("1+j")</item> returns 0.35+0.79j (rounded).
<bookmarkvalue>IMLOG10 function</bookmarkvalue>
IMLOG10
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMLOG10">The result is the common logarithm (to the base 10) of a complex number.</ahelp>
IMLOG10("ComplexNumber")
<item type="input">=IMLOG10("1+j")</item> returns 0.15+0.34j (rounded).
<bookmarkvalue>IMLOG2 function</bookmarkvalue>
IMLOG2
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMLOG2">The result is the binary logarithm of a complex number.</ahelp>
IMLOG2("ComplexNumber")
<item type="input">=IMLOG2("1+j")</item> returns 0.50+1.13j (rounded).
<bookmarkvalue>IMPRODUCT function</bookmarkvalue>
IMPRODUCT
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMPRODUCT">The result is the product of a set of complex numbers.</ahelp>
<item type="input">=IMPRODUCT("3+4j";"5-3j")</item> returns 27+11j.
<bookmarkvalue>IMREAL function</bookmarkvalue>
IMREAL
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMREAL">The result is the real coefficient of a complex number.</ahelp>
IMREAL("ComplexNumber")
<item type="input">=IMREAL("1+3j")</item> returns 1.

IMSUB
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMSUB">The result is the subtraction of two complex numbers.</ahelp>
IMSUB("ComplexNumber1"; "ComplexNumber2")
<item type="input">=IMSUB("13+4j";"5+3j")</item> returns 8+j.
<bookmarkvalue>IMSUM function</bookmarkvalue>
IMSUM
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMSUM">The result is the sum of a set of complex numbers.</ahelp>
<item type="input">=IMSUM("13+4j";"5+3j")</item> returns 18+7j.
<bookmarkvalue>IMSQRT function</bookmarkvalue>
IMSQRT
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCIMSQRT">The result is the square root of a complex number.</ahelp>
IMSQRT("ComplexNumber")
<item type="input">=IMSQRT("3+4i")</item> returns 2+1i.
<bookmarkvalue>COMPLEX function</bookmarkvalue>
COMPLEX
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCOMPLEX">The result is a complex number which is returned from a real coefficient and an imaginary coefficient.</ahelp>
COMPLEX(RealNum; INum [; Suffix])
<emph>RealNum</emph> is the real coefficient of the complex number.
<emph>INum</emph> is the imaginary coefficient of the complex number.
<emph>Suffix</emph> is a list of options, "i" or "j".
<item type="input">=COMPLEX(3;4;"j")</item> returns 3+4j.
<bookmarkvalue>OCT2BIN function</bookmarkvalue>         <bookmarkvalue>converting;octal numbers, into binary numbers</bookmarkvalue>
OCT2BIN
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCOCT2BIN">The result is the binary number for the octal number entered.</ahelp>
OCT2BIN(Number [; Places])
<emph>Number</emph> is the octal number. The number can have a maximum of 10 places. The most significant bit is the sign bit, the following bits return the value. Negative numbers are entered as two's complement.
<item type="input">=OCT2BIN(3;3)</item> returns 011.
<bookmarkvalue>OCT2DEC function</bookmarkvalue>         <bookmarkvalue>converting;octal numbers, into decimal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
OCT2DEC
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCOCT2DEZ">The result is the decimal number for the octal number entered.</ahelp>
OCT2DEC(Number)
<item type="input">=OCT2DEC(144)</item> returns 100.
<bookmarkvalue>OCT2HEX function</bookmarkvalue>         <bookmarkvalue>converting;octal numbers, into hexadecimal numbers</bookmarkvalue>
OCT2HEX
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCOCT2HEX"> The result is the hexadecimal number for the octal number entered.</ahelp>
OCT2HEX(Number [; Places])
<item type="input">=OCT2HEX(144;4)</item> returns 0064.
<bookmarkvalue>CONVERT function</bookmarkvalue>
CONVERT
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCONVERT">Converts a value from one unit of measure to the corresponding value in another unit of measure.</ahelp> Enter the units of measures directly as text in quotation marks or as a reference. If you enter the units of measure in cells, they must correspond exactly with the following list which is case sensitive: For example, in order to enter a lower case l (for liter) in a cell, enter the apostrophe ' immediately followed by l.
Property
Units
Weight
Length
Pressure
Force
Energy
Power
Field strength
<emph>T</emph>, <emph>ga</emph>
Temperature
Volume
Area
Speed
Information
<emph>bit</emph>, <emph>byte</emph>
Units of measure in <emph>bold</emph> can be preceded by a prefix character from the following list:
Prefix
Multiplier
Y (yotta)
10^24
Z (zetta)
10^21
E (exa)
10^18
P (peta)
10^15
T (tera)
10^12
G (giga)
10^9
M (mega)
10^6
k (kilo)
10^3
h (hecto)
10^2
e (deca)
10^1
d (deci)
10^-1
c (centi)
10^-2
m (milli)
10^-3
u (micro)
10^-6
n (nano)
10^-9
p (pico)
10^-12
f (femto)
10^-15
a (atto)
10^-18
z (zepto)
10^-21
y (yocto)
10^-24
Information units "bit" and "byte" may also be prefixed by one of the following IEC 60027-2 / IEEE 1541 prefixes:
CONVERT(Number; "FromUnit"; "ToUnit")
<emph>Number</emph> is the number to be converted.
<emph>FromUnit</emph> is the unit from which conversion is taking place.
<emph>ToUnit</emph> is the unit to which conversion is taking place. Both units must be of the same type.
<item type="input">=CONVERT(10;"HP";"PS") </item>returns, rounded to two decimal places, 10.14. 10 HP equal 10.14 PS.
<item type="input">=CONVERT(10;"km";"mi") </item>returns, rounded to two decimal places, 6.21. 10 kilometers equal 6.21 miles. The k is the permitted prefix character for the factor 10^3.
<bookmarkvalue>FACTDOUBLE function</bookmarkvalue>         <bookmarkvalue>factorials;numbers with increments of two</bookmarkvalue>
FACTDOUBLE
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCFACTDOUBLE">Returns the double factorial of a number.</ahelp>
FACTDOUBLE(Number)
Returns <emph>Number</emph>            <emph>!!</emph>, the double factorial of <emph>Number</emph>, where <emph>Number</emph> is an integer greater than or equal to zero.
For even numbers FACTDOUBLE(n) returns:
For odd numbers FACTDOUBLE(n) returns:
FACTDOUBLE(0) returns 1 by definition.
<item type="input">=FACTDOUBLE(5)</item> returns 15.
<item type="input">=FACTDOUBLE(6)</item> returns 48.
<item type="input">=FACTDOUBLE(0)</item> returns 1.
Financial Functions Part Three
<bookmarkvalue>ODDFPRICE function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>prices;securities with irregular first interest date</bookmarkvalue>
ODDFPRICE
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCODDFPRICE">Calculates the price per 100 currency units par value of a security, if the first interest date falls irregularly.</ahelp>
ODDFPRICE(Settlement; Maturity; Issue; FirstCoupon; Rate; Yield; Redemption; Frequency [; Basis])
<emph>Issue</emph> is the date of issue of the security.
<emph>FirstCoupon</emph> is the first interest date of the security.
<emph>Rate</emph> is the annual rate of interest.
<emph>Redemption</emph> is the redemption value per 100 currency units of par value.
<emph>Frequency</emph> is number of interest payments per year (1, 2 or 4).
<bookmarkvalue>ODDFYIELD function</bookmarkvalue>
ODDFYIELD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCODDFYIELD">Calculates the yield of a security if the first interest date falls irregularly.</ahelp>
ODDFYIELD(Settlement; Maturity; Issue; FirstCoupon; Rate; Price; Redemption; Frequency [; Basis])
<emph>FirstCoupon</emph> is the first interest period of the security.
<emph>Price</emph> is the price of the security.
<bookmarkvalue>ODDLPRICE function</bookmarkvalue>
ODDLPRICE
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCODDLPRICE">Calculates the price per 100 currency units par value of a security, if the last interest date falls irregularly.</ahelp>
ODDLPRICE(Settlement; Maturity; LastInterest; Rate; Yield; Redemption; Frequency [; Basis])
<emph>LastInterest</emph> is the last interest date of the security.
Settlement date: February 7 1999, maturity date: June 15 1999, last interest: October 15 1998. Interest rate: 3.75 per cent, yield: 4.05 per cent, redemption value: 100 currency units, frequency of payments: half-yearly = 2, basis: = 0
The price per 100 currency units per value of a security, which has an irregular last interest date, is calculated as follows:
=ODDLPRICE("1999-02-07";"1999-06-15";"1998-10-15"; 0.0375; 0.0405;100;2;0) returns 99.87829.
<bookmarkvalue>ODDLYIELD function</bookmarkvalue>
ODDLYIELD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCODDLYIELD">Calculates the yield of a security if the last interest date falls irregularly.</ahelp>
ODDLYIELD(Settlement; Maturity; LastInterest; Rate; Price; Redemption; Frequency [; Basis])
Settlement date: April 20 1999, maturity date: June 15 1999, last interest: October 15 1998. Interest rate: 3.75 per cent, price: 99.875 currency units, redemption value: 100 currency units, frequency of payments: half-yearly = 2, basis: = 0
The yield of the security, that has an irregular last interest date, is calculated as follows:
=ODDLYIELD("1999-04-20";"1999-06-15"; "1998-10-15"; 0.0375; 99.875; 100;2;0) returns 0.044873 or 4.4873%.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;variable declining depreciations</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>depreciations;variable declining</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>VDB function</bookmarkvalue>
VDB
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCVDB">Returns the depreciation of an asset for a specified or partial period using a variable declining balance method.</ahelp>
VDB(Cost; Salvage; Life; Start; End [; Factor [; NoSwitch]])
<emph>Cost</emph> is the initial value of an asset.
<emph>Life</emph> is the depreciation duration of the asset.
<emph>S</emph> is the start of the depreciation. A must be entered in the same date unit as the duration.
<emph>End</emph> is the end of the depreciation.
<emph>Factor</emph> (optional) is the depreciation factor. Factor = 2 is double rate depreciation.
<emph>NoSwitch</emph>is an optional parameter. NoSwitch = 0 (default) means a switch to linear depreciation. In NoSwitch = 1 no switch is made.
What is the declining-balance double-rate depreciation for a period if the initial cost is 35,000 currency units and the value at the end of the depreciation is 7,500 currency units. The depreciation period is 3 years. The depreciation from the 10th to the 20th period is calculated.
<item type="input">=VDB(35000;7500;36;10;20;2)</item> = 8603.80 currency units. The depreciation during the period between the 10th and the 20th period is 8,603.80 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;internal rates of return, irregular payments</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>internal rates of return;irregular payments</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>XIRR function</bookmarkvalue>
XIRR
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCXIRR">Calculates the internal rate of return for a list of payments which take place on different dates.</ahelp> The calculation is based on a 365 days per year basis, ignoring leap years.
If the payments take place at regular intervals, use the <link href="text/scalc/01/04060103.xhp#irr" name="IRR">IRR</link> function.
XIRR(Values; Dates [; Guess])
<emph>Values</emph> and <emph>Dates</emph> refer to a series of payments and the series of associated date values. The first pair of dates defines the start of the payment plan. All other date values must be later, but need not be in any order. The series of values must contain at least one negative and one positive value (receipts and deposits).
<emph>Guess</emph> (optional) is a guess that can be input for the internal rate of return. The default is 10%.
Calculation of the internal rate of return for the following five payments:
2001-01-01
-<item type="input">10000</item>
<item type="input">Received</item>
2001-01-02
<item type="input">2000</item>
<item type="input">Deposited</item>
2001-03-15
2500
2001-05-12
5000
2001-08-10
1000
=XIRR(B1:B5; A1:A5; 0.1) returns 0.1828.
<bookmarkvalue>XNPV function</bookmarkvalue>
XNPV
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCXNPV">Calculates the capital value (net present value) for a list of payments which take place on different dates.</ahelp> The calculation is based on a 365 days per year basis, ignoring leap years.
If the payments take place at regular intervals, use the <link href="text/scalc/01/04060119.xhp#npv" name="NPV">NPV</link> function.
XNPV(Rate; Values; Dates)
<emph>Rate</emph> is the internal rate of return for the payments.
<emph>Values</emph> and <emph>Dates</emph> refer to a series of payments and the series of associated date values. The first pair of dates defines the start of the payment plan. All other date values must be later, but need not be in any order. The series of values must contain at least one negative and one positive value (receipts and deposits)
Calculation of the net present value for the above-mentioned five payments for a national internal rate of return of 6%.
<item type="input">=XNPV(0.06;B1:B5;A1:A5)</item> returns 323.02.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;rates of return</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>RRI function</bookmarkvalue>
RRI
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZGZ">Calculates the interest rate resulting from the profit (return) of an investment.</ahelp>
RRI(P; PV; FV)
<emph>P</emph> is the number of periods needed for calculating the interest rate.
<emph>PV</emph> is the present (current) value. The cash value is the deposit of cash or the current cash value of an allowance in kind. As a deposit value a positive value must be entered; the deposit must not be 0 or <0.
<emph>FV</emph> determines what is desired as the cash value of the deposit.
For four periods (years) and a cash value of 7,500 currency units, the interest rate of the return is to be calculated if the future value is 10,000 currency units.
<item type="input">=RRI(4;7500;10000)</item> = 7.46 %
The interest rate must be 7.46 % so that 7,500 currency units will become 10,000 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;constant interest rates</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>constant interest rates</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>RATE function</bookmarkvalue>
RATE
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZINS">Returns the constant interest rate per period of an annuity.</ahelp>
RATE(NPer; Pmt; PV [ ; [ FV ] [ ; [ Type ] [ ; Guess ] ] ])
<emph>NPer</emph> is the total number of periods, during which payments are made (payment period).
<emph>Pmt</emph> is the constant payment (annuity) paid during each period.
<emph>PV</emph> is the cash value in the sequence of payments.
<emph>FV</emph> (optional) is the future value, which is reached at the end of the periodic payments.
<emph>Type</emph> (optional) is the due date of the periodic payment, either at the beginning or at the end of a period.
<emph>Guess</emph> (optional) determines the estimated value of the interest with iterative calculation.
What is the constant interest rate for a payment period of 3 periods if 10 currency units are paid regularly and the present cash value is 900 currency units.
<item type="input">=RATE(3;-10;900)</item> = -75.63% The interest rate is therefore 75.63%.
<bookmarkvalue>INTRATE function</bookmarkvalue>
INTRATE
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCINTRATE">Calculates the annual interest rate that results when a security (or other item) is purchased at an investment value and sold at a redemption value. No interest is paid.</ahelp>
INTRATE(Settlement; Maturity; Investment; Redemption [; Basis])
<emph>Maturity</emph> is the date on which the security is sold.
<emph>Investment</emph> is the purchase price.
<emph>Redemption</emph> is the selling price.
A painting is bought on 1990-01-15 for 1 million and sold on 2002-05-05 for 2 million. The basis is daily balance calculation (basis = 3). What is the average annual level of interest?
=INTRATE("1990-01-15"; "2002-05-05"; 1000000; 2000000; 3) returns 8.12%.
<bookmarkvalue>COUPNCD function</bookmarkvalue>
COUPNCD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCOUPNCD">Returns the date of the first interest date after the settlement date. Format the result as a date.</ahelp>
COUPNCD(Settlement; Maturity; Frequency [; Basis])
A security is purchased on 2001-01-25; the date of maturity is 2001-11-15. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). Using daily balance interest calculation (basis 3) when is the next interest date?
=COUPNCD("2001-01-25"; "2001-11-15"; 2; 3) returns 2001-05-15.
<bookmarkvalue>COUPDAYS function</bookmarkvalue>
COUPDAYS
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCOUPDAYS">Returns the number of days in the current interest period in which the settlement date falls.</ahelp>
COUPDAYS(Settlement; Maturity; Frequency [; Basis])
A security is purchased on 2001-01-25; the date of maturity is 2001-11-15. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). Using daily balance interest calculation (basis 3) how many days are there in the interest period in which the settlement date falls?
=COUPDAYS("2001-01-25"; "2001-11-15"; 2; 3) returns 181.
<bookmarkvalue>COUPDAYSNC function</bookmarkvalue>
COUPDAYSNC
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCOUPDAYSNC">Returns the number of days from the settlement date until the next interest date.</ahelp>
COUPDAYSNC(Settlement; Maturity; Frequency [; Basis])
<emph>Frequency </emph>is number of interest payments per year (1, 2 or 4).
A security is purchased on 2001-01-25; the date of maturity is 2001-11-15. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). Using daily balance interest calculation (basis 3) how many days are there until the next interest payment?
=COUPDAYSNC("2001-01-25"; "2001-11-15"; 2; 3) returns 110.
<bookmarkvalue>COUPDAYBS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>durations;first interest payment until settlement date</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>securities;first interest payment until settlement date</bookmarkvalue>
COUPDAYBS
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCOUPDAYBS">Returns the number of days from the first day of interest payment on a security until the settlement date.</ahelp>
COUPDAYBS(Settlement; Maturity; Frequency [; Basis])
A security is purchased on 2001-01-25; the date of maturity is 2001-11-15. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). Using daily balance interest calculation (basis 3) how many days is this?
=COUPDAYBS("2001-01-25"; "2001-11-15"; 2; 3) returns 71.
<bookmarkvalue>COUPPCD function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>dates;interest date prior to settlement date</bookmarkvalue>
COUPPCD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCOUPPCD">Returns the date of the interest date prior to the settlement date. Format the result as a date.</ahelp>
COUPPCD(Settlement; Maturity; Frequency [; Basis])
A security is purchased on 2001-01-25; the date of maturity is 2001-11-15. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). Using daily balance interest calculation (basis 3) what was the interest date prior to purchase?
=COUPPCD("2001-01-25"; "2001-11-15"; 2; 3) returns 2000-15-11.
<bookmarkvalue>COUPNUM function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>number of coupons</bookmarkvalue>
COUPNUM
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCOUPNUM">Returns the number of coupons (interest payments) between the settlement date and the maturity date.</ahelp>
COUPNUM(Settlement; Maturity; Frequency [; Basis])
A security is purchased on 2001-01-25; the date of maturity is 2001-11-15. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). Using daily balance interest calculation (basis 3) how many interest dates are there?
=COUPNUM("2001-01-25"; "2001-11-15"; 2; 3) returns 2.
<bookmarkvalue>IPMT function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>periodic amortizement rates</bookmarkvalue>
IPMT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZINSZ">Calculates the periodic amortizement for an investment with regular payments and a constant interest rate.</ahelp>
IPMT(Rate; Period; NPer; PV [; FV [; Type]])
<emph>Rate</emph> is the periodic interest rate.
<emph>Period</emph> is the period, for which the compound interest is calculated. Period=NPER if compound interest for the last period is calculated.
<emph>NPer</emph> is the total number of periods, during which annuity is paid.
<emph>PV</emph> is the present cash value in sequence of payments.
<emph>FV</emph> (optional) is the desired value (future value) at the end of the periods.
<emph>Type</emph> is the due date for the periodic payments.
What is the interest rate during the fifth period (year) if the constant interest rate is 5% and the cash value is 15,000 currency units? The periodic payment is seven years.
<item type="input">=IPMT(5%;5;7;15000)</item> = -352.97 currency units. The compound interest during the fifth period (year) is 352.97 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;future values</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>future values;constant interest rates</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>FV function</bookmarkvalue>
FV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZW">Returns the future value of an investment based on periodic, constant payments and a constant interest rate (Future Value).</ahelp>
FV(Rate; NPer; Pmt [ ; [ PV ] [ ; Type ] ])
<emph>Pmt</emph> is the annuity paid regularly per period.
<emph>PV</emph> (optional) is the (present) cash value of an investment.
<emph>Type</emph> (optional) defines whether the payment is due at the beginning or the end of a period.
What is the value at the end of an investment if the interest rate is 4% and the payment period is two years, with a periodic payment of 750 currency units. The investment has a present value of 2,500 currency units.
<item type="input">=FV(4%;2;750;2500) </item>= -4234.00 currency units. The value at the end of the investment is 4234.00 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>FVSCHEDULE function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>future values;varying interest rates</bookmarkvalue>
FVSCHEDULE
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCFVSCHEDULE">Calculates the accumulated value of the starting capital for a series of periodically varying interest rates.</ahelp>
FVSCHEDULE(Principal; Schedule)
<emph>Principal</emph> is the starting capital.
<emph>Schedule</emph> is a series of interest rates, for example, as a range H3:H5 or as a (List) (see example).
1000 currency units have been invested in for three years. The interest rates were 3%, 4% and 5% per annum. What is the value after three years?
<item type="input">=FVSCHEDULE(1000;{0.03;0.04;0.05})</item> returns 1124.76.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;number of payment periods</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>payment periods;number of</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>number of payment periods</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>NPER function</bookmarkvalue>
NPER
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZZR">Returns the number of periods for an investment based on periodic, constant payments and a constant interest rate.</ahelp>
NPER(Rate; Pmt; PV [ ; [ FV ] [ ; Type ] ])
<emph>Pmt</emph> is the constant annuity paid in each period.
<emph>PV</emph> is the present value (cash value) in a sequence of payments.
<emph>FV</emph> (optional) is the future value, which is reached at the end of the last period.
<emph>Type</emph> (optional) is the due date of the payment at the beginning or at the end of the period.
How many payment periods does a payment period cover with a periodic interest rate of 6%, a periodic payment of 153.75 currency units and a present cash value of 2.600 currency units.
<item type="input">=NPER(6%;153.75;2600)</item> = -12,02. The payment period covers 12.02 periods.

Financial Functions Part Two

<bookmarkvalue>PPMT function</bookmarkvalue>
PPMT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCKAPZ">Returns for a given period the payment on the principal for an investment that is based on periodic and constant payments and a constant interest rate.</ahelp>
PPMT(Rate; Period; NPer; PV [ ; FV [ ; Type ] ])
<emph>Period</emph> is the amortizement period. P = 1 for the first and P = NPer for the last period.
<emph>NPer</emph> is the total number of periods during which annuity is paid.
<emph>PV</emph> is the present value in the sequence of payments.
<emph>FV</emph> (optional) is the desired (future) value.
<emph>Type</emph> (optional) defines the due date. F = 1 for payment at the beginning of a period and F = 0 for payment at the end of a period.
How high is the periodic monthly payment at an annual interest rate of 8.75% over a period of 3 years? The cash value is 5,000 currency units and is always paid at the beginning of a period. The future value is 8,000 currency units.
<item type="input">=PPMT(8.75%/12;1;36;5000;8000;1)</item> = -350.99 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating; total amortizement rates</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>total amortizement rates</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>amortization installment</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>repayment installment</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>CUMPRINC function</bookmarkvalue>
CUMPRINC
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCKUMKAPITAL">Returns the cumulative interest paid for an investment period with a constant interest rate.</ahelp>
CUMPRINC(Rate; NPer; PV; S; E; Type)
<emph>NPer</emph> is the payment period with the total number of periods. NPER can also be a non-integer value.
<emph>PV</emph> is the current value in the sequence of payments.
<emph>S</emph> is the first period.
<emph>E</emph> is the last period.
<emph>Type</emph> is the due date of the payment at the beginning or end of each period.
What are the payoff amounts if the yearly interest rate is 5.5% for 36 months? The cash value is 15,000 currency units. The payoff amount is calculated between the 10th and 18th period. The due date is at the end of the period.
<item type="input">=CUMPRINC(5.5%/12;36;15000;10;18;0)</item> = -3669.74 currency units. The payoff amount between the 10th and 18th period is 3669.74 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>CUMPRINCADD function</bookmarkvalue>
CUMPRINCADD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCUMPRINC"> Calculates the cumulative redemption of a loan in a period.</ahelp>
CUMPRINCADD(Rate; NPer; PV; StartPeriod; EndPeriod; Type)
<emph>Rate</emph> is the interest rate for each period.
<emph>NPer</emph> is the total number of payment periods. The rate and NPER must refer to the same unit, and thus both be calculated annually or monthly.
<emph>PV</emph> is the current value.
<emph>StartPeriod</emph> is the first payment period for the calculation.
<emph>EndPeriod</emph> is the last payment period for the calculation.
<emph>Type</emph> is the maturity of a payment at the end of each period (Type = 0) or at the start of the period (Type = 1).
The following mortgage loan is taken out on a house:
Rate: 9.00 per cent per annum (9% / 12 = 0.0075), Duration: 30 years (payment periods = 30 * 12 = 360), NPV: 125000 currency units.
How much will you repay in the second year of the mortgage (thus from periods 13 to 24)?
<item type="input">=CUMPRINCADD(0.0075;360;125000;13;24;0)</item> returns -934.1071
In the first month you will be repaying the following amount:
<item type="input">=CUMPRINCADD(0.0075;360;125000;1;1;0)</item> returns -68.27827
<bookmarkvalue>calculating; accumulated interests</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>accumulated interests</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>CUMIPMT function</bookmarkvalue>
CUMIPMT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCKUMZINSZ">Calculates the cumulative interest payments, that is, the total interest, for an investment based on a constant interest rate.</ahelp>
CUMIPMT(Rate; NPer; PV; S; E; Type)
What are the interest payments at a yearly interest rate of 5.5 %, a payment period of monthly payments for 2 years and a current cash value of 5,000 currency units? The start period is the 4th and the end period is the 6th period. The payment is due at the beginning of each period.
<item type="input">=CUMIPMT(5.5%/12;24;5000;4;6;1)</item> = -57.54 currency units. The interest payments for between the 4th and 6th period are 57.54 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>CUMIPMTADD function</bookmarkvalue>
CUMIPMTADD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCCUMIPMT">Calculates the accumulated interest for a period.</ahelp>
CUMIPMTADD(Rate; NPer; PV; StartPeriod; EndPeriod; Type)
Rate: 9.00 per cent per annum (9% / 12 = 0.0075), Duration: 30 years (NPER = 30 * 12 = 360), Pv: 125000 currency units.
How much interest must you pay in the second year of the mortgage (thus from periods 13 to 24)?
<item type="input">=CUMIPMTADD(0.0075;360;125000;13;24;0)</item> returns -11135.23.
How much interest must you pay in the first month?
<item type="input">=CUMIPMTADD(0.0075;360;125000;1;1;0)</item> returns -937.50.
<bookmarkvalue>PRICE function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>prices; fixed interest securities</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>sales values;fixed interest securities</bookmarkvalue>
PRICE
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCPRICE">Calculates the market value of a fixed interest security with a par value of 100 currency units as a function of the forecast yield.</ahelp>
PRICE(Settlement; Maturity; Rate; Yield; Redemption; Frequency [; Basis])
<emph>Rate</emph> is the annual nominal rate of interest (coupon interest rate)
A security is purchased on 1999-02-15; the maturity date is 2007-11-15. The nominal rate of interest is 5.75%. The yield is 6.5%. The redemption value is 100 currency units. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). With calculation on basis 0, the price is as follows:
<input>=PRICE("1999-02-15"; "2007-11-15"; 0.0575; 0.065; 100; 2; 0)</input>  returns 95.04287.
<bookmarkvalue>PRICEDISC function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>prices;non-interest-bearing securities</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>sales values;non-interest-bearing securities</bookmarkvalue>
PRICEDISC
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCPRICEDISC">Calculates the price per 100 currency units of par value of a non-interest- bearing security.</ahelp>
PRICEDISC(Settlement; Maturity; Discount; Redemption [; Basis])
<emph>Discount</emph> is the discount of a security as a percentage.
A security is purchased on 1999-02-15; the maturity date is 1999-03-01. Discount in per cent is 5.25%. The redemption value is 100. When calculating on basis 2 the price discount is as follows:
<input>=PRICEDISC("1999-02-15"; "1999-03-01"; 0.0525; 100; 2)</input>  returns 99.79583.
<bookmarkvalue>PRICEMAT function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>prices;interest-bearing securities</bookmarkvalue>
PRICEMAT
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCPRICEMAT">Calculates the price per 100 currency units of par value of a security, that pays interest on the maturity date.</ahelp>
PRICEMAT(Settlement; Maturity; Issue; Rate; Yield [; Basis])
<emph>Rate</emph> is the interest rate of the security on the issue date.
Settlement date: February 15 1999, maturity date: April 13 1999, issue date: November 11 1998. Interest rate: 6.1 per cent, yield: 6.1 per cent, basis: 30/360 = 0.
The price is calculated as follows:
<input>=PRICEMAT("1999-02-15";"1999-04-13";"1998-11-11"; 0.061; 0.061;0)</input>  returns 99.98449888.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating; durations</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>durations;calculating</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>PDURATION function</bookmarkvalue>
PDURATION
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCLAUFZEIT">Calculates the number of periods required by an investment to attain the desired value.</ahelp>
PDURATION(Rate; PV; FV)
<emph>Rate</emph> is a constant. The interest rate is to be calculated for the entire duration (duration period). The interest rate per period is calculated by dividing the interest rate by the calculated duration. The internal rate for an annuity is to be entered as Rate/12.
<emph>FV</emph> is the expected value. The future value determines the desired (future) value of the deposit.
At an interest rate of 4.75%, a cash value of 25,000 currency units and a future value of 1,000,000 currency units, a duration of 79.49 payment periods is returned. The periodic payment is the resulting quotient from the future value and the duration, in this case 1,000,000/79.49=12,850.20.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;linear depreciations</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>depreciations;linear</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>linear depreciations</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>straight-line depreciations</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>SLN function</bookmarkvalue>
SLN
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCLIA">Returns the straight-line depreciation of an asset for one period.</ahelp> The amount of the depreciation is constant during the depreciation period.
SLN(Cost; Salvage; Life)
<emph>Life</emph> is the depreciation period determining the number of periods in the depreciation of the asset.
Office equipment with an initial cost of 50,000 currency units is to be depreciated over 7 years. The value at the end of the depreciation is to be 3,500 currency units.
<item type="input">=SLN(50000;3,500;84)</item> = 553.57 currency units. The periodic monthly depreciation of the office equipment is 553.57 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>MDURATION function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>Macauley duration</bookmarkvalue>
MDURATION
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCMDURATION">Calculates the modified Macauley duration of a fixed interest security in years.</ahelp>
MDURATION(Settlement; Maturity; Coupon; Yield; Frequency [; Basis])
<emph>Coupon</emph> is the annual nominal rate of interest (coupon interest rate)
A security is purchased on 2001-01-01; the maturity date is 2006-01-01. The nominal rate of interest is 8%. The yield is 9.0%. Interest is paid half-yearly (frequency is 2). Using daily balance interest calculation (basis 3) how long is the modified duration?
<input>=MDURATION("2001-01-01"; "2006-01-01"; 0.08; 0.09; 2; 3)</input> returns 4.02 years.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;net present values</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>net present values</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>NPV function</bookmarkvalue>
NPV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCNBW">Returns the present value of an investment based on a series of periodic cash flows and a discount rate. To get the net present value, subtract the cost of the project (the initial cash flow at time zero) from the returned value.</ahelp>
If the payments take place at irregular intervals, use the <link href="text/scalc/01/04060118.xhp#xnpv" name="XNPV">XNPV</link> function.
NPV(Rate; <embedvar href="text/scalc/01/fulfunc.xhp#number2541" markup="keep"/>)
<emph>Rate</emph> is the discount rate for a period.
What is the net present value of periodic payments of 10, 20 and 30 currency units with a discount rate of 8.75%. At time zero the costs were paid as -40 currency units.
<item type="input">=NPV(8.75%;10;20;30)</item> = 49.43 currency units. The net present value is the returned value minus the initial costs of 40 currency units, therefore 9.43 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;nominal interest rates</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>nominal interest rates</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>NOMINAL function</bookmarkvalue>
NOMINAL
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCNOMINAL">Calculates the yearly nominal interest rate, given the effective rate and the number of compounding periods per year.</ahelp>
NOMINAL(EffectiveRate; NPerY)
<emph>EffectiveRate</emph> is the effective interest rate
<emph>NPerY</emph> is the number of periodic interest payments per year.
What is the nominal interest per year for an effective interest rate of 13.5% if twelve payments are made per year.
<item type="input">=NOMINAL(13.5%;12)</item> = 12.73%. The nominal interest rate per year is 12.73%.
<bookmarkvalue>NOMINALADD function</bookmarkvalue>
NOMINALADD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCNOMINAL">Calculates the annual nominal rate of interest on the basis of the effective rate and the number of interest payments per annum.</ahelp>
NOMINALADD(EffectiveRate; NPerY)
<emph>EffectiveRate</emph> is the effective annual rate of interest.
<emph>NPerY</emph> the number of interest payments per year.
What is the nominal rate of interest for a 5.3543% effective rate of interest and quarterly payment.
<item type="input">=NOMINALADD(5.3543%;4)</item> returns 0.0525 or 5.25%.
<bookmarkvalue>DOLLARFR function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>converting;decimal fractions, into mixed decimal fractions</bookmarkvalue>
DOLLARFR
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCDOLLARFR">Converts a quotation that has been given as a decimal number into a mixed decimal fraction.</ahelp>
DOLLARFR(DecimalDollar; Fraction)
<emph>DecimalDollar</emph> is a decimal number.
<emph>Fraction</emph> is a whole number that is used as the denominator of the decimal fraction.
<item type="input">=DOLLARFR(1.125;16)</item> converts into sixteenths. The result is 1.02 for 1 plus 2/16.
<item type="input">=DOLLARFR(1.125;8)</item> converts into eighths. The result is 1.1 for 1 plus 1/8.
<bookmarkvalue>fractions; converting</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>converting;decimal fractions, into decimal numbers</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>DOLLARDE function</bookmarkvalue>
DOLLARDE

DOLLARDE(FractionalDollar; Fraction)
<emph>FractionalDollar</emph> is a number given as a decimal fraction.

<item type="input">=DOLLARDE(1.1;8)</item> stands for 1 and 1/8. This returns 1.125.
<bookmarkvalue>calculating;modified internal rates of return</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>modified internal rates of return</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>MIRR function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>internal rates of return;modified</bookmarkvalue>
MIRR
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCQIKV">Calculates the modified internal rate of return of a series of investments.</ahelp>
MIRR(Values; Investment; ReinvestRate)
<emph>Values</emph> corresponds to the array or the cell reference for cells whose content corresponds to the payments.
<emph>Investment</emph> is the rate of interest of the investments (the negative values of the array)
<emph>ReinvestRate</emph>:the rate of interest of the reinvestment (the positive values of the array)
Assuming a cell content of A1 = <item type="input">-5</item>, A2 = <item type="input">10</item>, A3 = <item type="input">15</item>, and A4 = <item type="input">8</item>, and an investment value of 0.5 and a reinvestment value of 0.1, the result is 94.16%.
<bookmarkvalue>YIELD function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>rates of return;securities</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>yields, see also rates of return</bookmarkvalue>
YIELD
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCYIELD">Calculates the yield of a security.</ahelp>
YIELD(Settlement; Maturity; Rate; Price; Redemption; Frequency [; Basis])
<emph>Price</emph> is the price (purchase price) of the security per 100 currency units of par value.

<input>=YIELD("1999-02-15"; "2007-11-15"; 0.0575 ;95.04287; 100; 2; 0)</input>  returns 0.065 or 6.50 per cent.

<bookmarkvalue>calculating;annuities</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>annuities</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>PMT function</bookmarkvalue>
PMT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCRMZ">Returns the periodic payment for an annuity with constant interest rates.</ahelp>
PMT(Rate; NPer; PV [ ; [ FV ] [ ; Type ] ])
<emph>NPer</emph> is the number of periods in which annuity is paid.
<emph>FV</emph> (optional) is the desired value (future value) to be reached at the end of the periodic payments.
<emph>Type</emph> (optional) is the due date for the periodic payments. Type=1 is payment at the beginning and Type=0 is payment at the end of each period.
What are the periodic payments at a yearly interest rate of 1.99% if the payment time is 3 years and the cash value is 25,000 currency units. There are 36 months as 36 payment periods, and the interest rate per payment period is 1.99%/12.
<item type="input">=PMT(1.99%/12;36;25000)</item> = -715.96 currency units. The periodic monthly payment is therefore 715.96 currency units.
<bookmarkvalue>TBILLEQ function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>treasury bills;annual return</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>annual return on treasury bills</bookmarkvalue>
TBILLEQ

TBILLEQ(Settlement; Maturity; Discount)
Settlement date: March 31 1999, maturity date: June 1 1999, discount: 9.14 per cent.
The return on the treasury bill corresponding to a security is worked out as follows:
<input>=TBILLEQ("1999-03-31";"1999-06-01"; 0.0914)</input>  returns 0.094151 or 9.4151 per cent.

Bit Operation Functions
<bookmarkvalue>BITAND function</bookmarkvalue>
BITAND
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBITAND">Returns a bitwise logical "and" of the parameters.</ahelp>
BITAND(number1; number2)
<emph>Number1</emph> and <emph>number2</emph> are positive integers less than 2 ^ 48 (281 474 976 710 656).
<item type="input">=BITAND(6;10)</item> returns 2 (0110  1010 = 0010).
<bookmarkvalue>BITOR function</bookmarkvalue>
BITOR
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBITOR">Returns a bitwise logical "or" of the parameters.</ahelp>
BITOR(number1; number2)
<item type="input">=BITOR(6;10)</item> returns 14  (0110 | 1010 = 1110).
<bookmarkvalue>BITXOR function</bookmarkvalue>
BITXOR
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBITXOR">Returns a bitwise logical "exclusive or" of the parameters.</ahelp>
BITXOR(number1; number2)
<item type="input">=BITXOR(6;10)</item> returns  12 (0110 ^ 1010 = 1100)
<bookmarkvalue>BITLSHIFT function</bookmarkvalue>
BITLSHIFT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBITLSHIFT">Shifts a number left by n bits.</ahelp>
BITLSHIFT(number; shift)
<emph>Number</emph> is a positive integer less than 2 ^ 48 (281 474 976 710 656).
<emph>Shift</emph> is the number of positions the bits will be moved to the left. If shift is negative, it is synonymous with BITRSHIFT (number; -shift).
<item type="input">=BITLSHIFT(6;1)</item> returns 12 (0110 << 1 = 1100).
<bookmarkvalue>BITRSHIFT function</bookmarkvalue>
BITRSHIFT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBITRSHIFT">Shifts a number right by n bits.</ahelp>
BITRSHIFT(number; shift)
<emph>Shift</emph> is the number of positions the bits will be moved to the right. If shift is negative, it is synonymous with BITLSHIFT (number; -shift).
<item type="input">=BITRSHIFT(6;1)</item> returns 3 (0110 >> 1 = 0011).
Statistical Functions Part One

<bookmarkvalue>INTERCEPT function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>points of intersection</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>intersections</bookmarkvalue>
INTERCEPT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCACHSENABSCHNITT">Calculates the point at which a line will intersect the y-values by using known x-values and y-values.</ahelp>
INTERCEPT(DataY; DataX)
<emph>DataY</emph> is the dependent set of observations or data.
<emph>DataX</emph> is the independent set of observations or data.
Names, arrays or references containing numbers must be used here. Numbers can also be entered directly.
To calculate the intercept, use cells D3:D9 as the y value and C3:C9 as the x value from the example spreadsheet. Input will be as follows:
<item type="input">=INTERCEPT(D3:D9;C3:C9)</item> = 2.15.
<bookmarkvalue>COUNT function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>numbers;counting</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="counthead"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060181.xhp#count">COUNT</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCANZAHL">Counts how many numbers are in the list of arguments.</ahelp> Text entries are ignored.
COUNT(<embedvar href="text/scalc/01/fulfunc.xhp#number2551" markup="keep"/>)
The entries 2, 4, 6 and eight in the Value 1-4 fields are to be counted.
<item type="input">=COUNT(2;4;6;"eight")</item> = 3. The count of numbers is therefore 3.
<bookmarkvalue>COUNTA function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>number of entries</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="countahead"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060181.xhp#counta">COUNTA</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCANZAHL2">Counts how many values are in the list of arguments.</ahelp> Text entries are also counted, even when they contain an empty string of length 0. If an argument is an array or reference, empty cells within the array or reference are ignored.
COUNTA(<embedvar href="text/scalc/01/fulfunc.xhp#number2551" markup="keep"/>)
<item type="input">=COUNTA(2;4;6;"eight")</item> = 4. The count of values is therefore 4.
<bookmarkvalue>COUNTBLANK function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>counting;empty cells</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>empty cells;counting</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="countblankhead"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060181.xhp#countblank">COUNTBLANK</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCANZAHLLEEREZELLEN">Returns the number of empty cells.</ahelp>
COUNTBLANK(Range)
Returns the number of empty cells in the cell range <emph>Range</emph>.
<item type="input">=COUNTBLANK(A1:B2)</item> returns 4 if cells A1, A2, B1, and B2 are all empty.
<bookmarkvalue>COUNTIF function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>counting;specified cells</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="countifhead"><link href="text/scalc/01/04060181.xhp#countif">COUNTIF</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZAEHLENWENN">Returns the number of cells that meet with certain criteria within a cell range.</ahelp>
COUNTIF(Range; Criteria)
<emph>Criteria</emph> indicates the criteria in the form of a number, an expression or a character string. These criteria determine which cells are counted.
A1:A10 is a cell range containing the numbers <item type="input">2000</item> to <item type="input">2009</item>. Cell B1 contains the number <item type="input">2006</item>. In cell B2, you enter a formula:
<item type="input">=COUNTIF(A1:A10;2006)</item> - this returns 1.
<item type="input">=COUNTIF(A1:A10;B1)</item> - this returns 1.
<item type="input">=COUNTIF(A1:A10;">=2006")</item> - this returns 4.
<item type="input">=COUNTIF(A1:A10;"<"B1)</item> - when B1 contains <item type="input">2006</item>, this returns 6.
<item type="input">=COUNTIF(A1:A10;C2)</item> where cell C2 contains the text <item type="input">>2006</item> counts the number of cells in the range A1:A10 which are >2006.
To count only negative numbers: <item type="input">=COUNTIF(A1:A10;"<0")</item>
<bookmarkvalue>B function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>probabilities of samples with binomial distribution</bookmarkvalue>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCB">Returns the probability of a sample with binomial distribution.</ahelp>
<emph>Trials</emph> is the number of independent trials.
<emph>SP</emph> is the probability of success on each trial.
<emph>T1</emph> defines the lower limit for the number of trials.
<emph>T2</emph> (optional) defines the upper limit for the number of trials.
What is the probability with ten throws of the dice, that a six will come up exactly twice? The probability of a six (or any other number) is 1/6. The following formula combines these factors:
<item type="input">=B(10;1/6;2)</item> returns a probability of 29%.
<bookmarkvalue>RSQ function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>determination coefficients</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>regression analysis</bookmarkvalue>
RSQ
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBESTIMMTHEITSMASS">Returns the square of the Pearson correlation coefficient based on the given values.</ahelp> RSQ (also called determination coefficient) is a measure for the accuracy of an adjustment and can be used to produce a regression analysis.
RSQ(DataY; DataX)
<emph>DataY</emph> is an array or range of data points.
<emph>DataX</emph> is an array or range of data points.
<item type="input">=RSQ(A1:A20;B1:B20)</item> calculates the determination coefficient for both data sets in columns A and B.
<bookmarkvalue>BETAINV function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>cumulative probability density function;inverse of</bookmarkvalue>
BETAINV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBETAINV">Returns the inverse of the cumulative beta probability density function.</ahelp>
BETAINV(Number; Alpha; Beta [; Start [; End]])
<emph>Number</emph> is the value between <emph>Start</emph> and <emph>End</emph> at which to evaluate the function.
<emph>Alpha</emph> is a parameter to the distribution.
<emph>Beta</emph> is a parameter to the distribution.
<emph>Start</emph> (optional) is the lower bound for <emph>Number</emph>.
<emph>End</emph> (optional) is the upper bound for <emph>Number</emph>.
<item type="input">=BETAINV(0.5;5;10)</item> returns the value 0.33.

BETA.INV(Number; Alpha; Beta [; Start [; End]])
<item type="input">=BETA.INV(0.5;5;10)</item> returns the value 0.3257511553.
<bookmarkvalue>BETADIST function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>cumulative probability density function;calculating</bookmarkvalue>
BETADIST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBETAVERT">Returns the beta function.</ahelp>
BETADIST(Number; Alpha; Beta [; Start [; End [; Cumulative]]])
<emph>Cumulative</emph> (optional) can be 0 or False to calculate the probability density function. It can be any other value or True or omitted to calculate the cumulative distribution function.
<item type="input">=BETADIST(0.75;3;4)</item> returns the value 0.96.
<bookmarkvalue>BETA.DIST function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>cumulative probability density function;calculating</bookmarkvalue>
BETA.DIST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBETADISTMS">Returns the beta function.</ahelp>
BETA.DIST(Number; Alpha; Beta; Cumulative [; Start [; End]])
<emph>Number</emph> (required) is the value between <emph>Start</emph> and <emph>End</emph> at which to evaluate the function.
<emph>Alpha</emph> (required) is a parameter to the distribution.
<emph>Beta</emph> (required) is a parameter to the distribution.
<emph>Cumulative</emph> (required) can be 0 or False to calculate the probability density function. It can be any other value or True to calculate the cumulative distribution function.
<item type="input">=BETA.DIST(2;8;10;1;1;3)</item> returns the value 0.6854706
<item type="input">=BETA.DIST(2;8;10;0;1;3)</item> returns the value 1.4837646
<bookmarkvalue>BINOMDIST function</bookmarkvalue>
BINOMDIST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBINOMVERT">Returns the individual term binomial distribution probability.</ahelp>
BINOMDIST(X; Trials; SP; C)
<emph>X</emph> is the number of successes in a set of trials.
<emph>C</emph> = 0 calculates the probability of a single event and <emph>C</emph> = 1 calculates the cumulative probability.
<item type="input">=BINOMDIST(A1;12;0.5;0)</item> shows (if the values <item type="input">0</item> to <item type="input">12</item> are entered in A1) the probabilities for 12 flips of a coin that <emph>Heads</emph> will come up exactly the number of times entered in A1.
<item type="input">=BINOMDIST(A1;12;0.5;1)</item> shows the cumulative probabilities for the same series. For example, if A1 = <item type="input">4</item>, the cumulative probability of the series is 0, 1, 2, 3 or 4 times <emph>Heads</emph> (non-exclusive OR).
<bookmarkvalue>BINOM.DIST function</bookmarkvalue>
BINOM.DIST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBINOMDISTMS">Returns the individual term binomial distribution probability.</ahelp>
BINOM.DIST(X; Trials; SP; C)
<item type="input">=BINOM.DIST(A1;12;0.5;0)</item> shows (if the values <item type="input">0</item> to <item type="input">12</item> are entered in A1) the probabilities for 12 flips of a coin that <emph>Heads</emph> will come up exactly the number of times entered in A1.
<item type="input">=BINOM.DIST(A1;12;0.5;1)</item> shows the cumulative probabilities for the same series. For example, if A1 = <item type="input">4</item>, the cumulative probability of the series is 0, 1, 2, 3 or 4 times <emph>Heads</emph> (non-exclusive OR).
<bookmarkvalue>BINOM.INV function</bookmarkvalue>
BINOM.INV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCBINOMINVMS">Returns the smallest value for which the cumulative binomial distribution is greater than or equal to a criterion value.</ahelp>
BINOM.INV(Trials; SP; Alpha)
<emph>Trials</emph> The total number of trials.
<emph>Alpha</emph> The border probability that is attained or exceeded.
<item type="input">=BINOM.INV(8;0.6;0.9)</item> returns 7, the smallest value for which the cumulative binomial distribution is greater than or equal to a criterion value.

CHISQINV(Probability; Degrees of Freedom)

CHISQ.INV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHISQINVMS">Returns the inverse of the left-tailed probability of the chi-square distribution.</ahelp>
CHISQ.INV(Probability; DegreesFreedom)
<item type="input">=CHISQ.INV(0,5;1)</item> returns 0.4549364231.
<bookmarkvalue>CHIINV function</bookmarkvalue>
CHIINV
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHIINV">Returns the inverse of the one-tailed probability of the chi-squared distribution.</ahelp>
CHIINV(Number; DegreesFreedom)
<emph>Number</emph> is the value of the error probability.
<emph>DegreesFreedom</emph> is the degrees of freedom of the experiment.
A die is thrown 1020 times. The numbers on the die 1 through 6 come up 195, 151, 148, 189, 183 and 154 times (observation values). The hypothesis that the die is not fixed is to be tested.
The Chi square distribution of the random sample is determined by the formula given above. Since the expected value for a given number on the die for n throws is n times 1/6, thus 1020/6 = 170, the formula returns a Chi square value of 13.27.
If the (observed) Chi square is greater than or equal to the (theoretical) Chi square CHIINV, the hypothesis will be discarded, since the deviation between theory and experiment is too great. If the observed Chi square is less that CHIINV, the hypothesis is confirmed with the indicated probability of error.
<item type="input">=CHIINV(0.05;5)</item> returns 11.07.
<item type="input">=CHIINV(0.02;5)</item> returns 13.39.
If the probability of error is 5%, the die is not true. If the probability of error is 2%, there is no reason to believe it is fixed.
<bookmarkvalue>CHISQ.INV.RT function</bookmarkvalue>
CHISQ.INV.RT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHIINVMS">Returns the inverse of the one-tailed probability of the chi-squared distribution.</ahelp>
CHISQ.INV.RT(Number; DegreesFreedom)
<item type="input">=CHISQ.INV.RT(0.05;5)</item> returns 11.0704976935.
<item type="input">=CHISQ.INV.RT(0.02;5)</item> returns 13.388222599.
<bookmarkvalue>CHITEST function</bookmarkvalue>
CHITEST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHITEST">Returns the probability of a deviance from a random distribution of two test series based on the chi-squared test for independence.</ahelp> CHITEST returns the chi-squared distribution of the data.
The probability determined by CHITEST can also be determined with CHIDIST, in which case the Chi square of the random sample must then be passed as a parameter instead of the data row.
CHITEST(DataB; DataE)
<emph>DataB</emph> is the array of the observations.
<emph>DataE</emph> is the range of the expected values.
DataB (observed)
DataE (expected)
<item type="input">195</item>
<item type="input">170</item>
<item type="input">151</item>
<item type="input">148</item>
<item type="input">189</item>
<item type="input">183</item>
<item type="input">154</item>
<item type="input">=CHITEST(A1:A6;B1:B6)</item> equals 0.02. This is the probability which suffices the observed data of the theoretical Chi-square distribution.
<bookmarkvalue>CHISQ.TEST function</bookmarkvalue>
CHISQ.TEST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHITESTMS">Returns the probability of a deviance from a random distribution of two test series based on the chi-squared test for independence.</ahelp> CHISQ.TEST returns the chi-squared distribution of the data.
The probability determined by CHISQ.TEST can also be determined with CHISQ.DIST, in which case the Chi square of the random sample must then be passed as a parameter instead of the data row.
CHISQ.TEST(DataB; DataE)
<item type="input">=CHISQ.TEST(A1:A6;B1:B6)</item> equals 0.0209708029. This is the probability which suffices the observed data of the theoretical Chi-square distribution.
<bookmarkvalue>CHIDIST function</bookmarkvalue>
CHIDIST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHIVERT">Returns the probability value from the indicated Chi square that a hypothesis is confirmed.</ahelp> CHIDIST compares the Chi square value to be given for a random sample that is calculated from the sum of (observed value-expected value)^2/expected value for all values with the theoretical Chi square distribution and determines from this the probability of error for the hypothesis to be tested.
The probability determined by CHIDIST can also be determined by CHITEST.
CHIDIST(Number; DegreesFreedom)
<emph>Number</emph> is the chi-square value of the random sample used to determine the error probability.
<emph>DegreesFreedom</emph> are the degrees of freedom of the experiment.
<item type="input">=CHIDIST(13.27; 5)</item> equals 0.02.
If the Chi square value of the random sample is 13.27 and if the experiment has 5 degrees of freedom, then the hypothesis is assured with a probability of error of 2%.
<bookmarkvalue>CHISQ.DIST function</bookmarkvalue>
CHISQ.DIST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHISQDISTMS">Returns the probability density function or the cumulative distribution function for the chi-square distribution.</ahelp>
CHISQ.DIST(Number; DegreesFreedom; Cumulative)
<emph>Cumulative</emph> can be 0 or False to calculate the probability density function. It can be any other value or True to calculate the cumulative distribution function.
<item type="input">=CHISQ.DIST(3; 2; 0) </item>equals 0.1115650801, the probability density function with 2 degrees of freedom, at x = 3.
<item type="input">=CHISQ.DIST(3; 2; 1) </item>equals 0.7768698399, the cumulative chi-square distribution with 2 degrees of freedom, at the value x = 3.
<bookmarkvalue>CHISQ.DIST.RT function</bookmarkvalue>
CHISQ.DIST.RT
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCHIVERTMS">Returns the probability value from the indicated Chi square that a hypothesis is confirmed.</ahelp> CHISQ.DIST.RT compares the Chi square value to be given for a random sample that is calculated from the sum of (observed value-expected value)^2/expected value for all values with the theoretical Chi square distribution and determines from this the probability of error for the hypothesis to be tested.
The probability determined by CHISQ.DIST.RT can also be determined by CHITEST.
CHISQ.DIST.RT(Number; DegreesFreedom)
<item type="input">=CHISQ.DIST.RT(13.27; 5)</item> equals 0.0209757694.
<bookmarkvalue>CHISQDIST function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>chi-square distribution</bookmarkvalue>
CHISQDIST
<ahelp hid=".">Returns the value of the probability density function or the cumulative distribution function for the chi-square distribution.</ahelp>
CHISQDIST(Number; Degrees Of Freedom [; Cumulative])
<emph>Number</emph> is the number for which the function is to be calculated.
<emph>Cumulative</emph> (optional): 0 or False calculates the probability density function. Other values or True or omitted calculates the cumulative distribution function.

EXPONDIST

EXPONDIST(Number; Lambda; C)
<emph>Number</emph> is the value of the function.
<emph>Lambda</emph> is the parameter value.
<emph>C</emph> is a logical value that determines the form of the function. <emph>C = 0</emph> calculates the density function, and <emph>C = 1</emph> calculates the distribution.
<item type="input">=EXPONDIST(3;0.5;1)</item> returns 0.78.

<bookmarkvalue>TRIMMEAN function</bookmarkvalue>         <bookmarkvalue>means;of data set without margin data</bookmarkvalue>
TRIMMEAN
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCGESTUTZTMITTEL">Returns the mean of a data set without the Alpha percent of data at the margins.</ahelp>
TRIMMEAN(Data; Alpha)
<emph>Data</emph> is the array of data in the sample.
<emph>Alpha</emph> is the percentage of the marginal data that will not be taken into consideration.
<item type="input">=TRIMMEAN(A1:A50; 0.1)</item> calculates the mean value of numbers in A1:A50, without taking into consideration the 5 percent of the values representing the highest values and the 5 percent of the values representing the lowest ones. The percentage numbers refer to the amount of the untrimmed mean value, not to the number of summands.
<bookmarkvalue>ZTEST function</bookmarkvalue>
ZTEST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCGTEST">Calculates the probability of observing a z-statistic greater than the one computed based on a sample.</ahelp>
ZTEST(Data; mu [; Sigma])
<emph>Data</emph> is the given sample, drawn from a normally distributed population.
<emph>mu</emph> is the known mean of the population.
<emph>Sigma</emph> (optional) is the known standard deviation of the population. If omitted, the standard deviation of the given sample is used.
See also the <link href="https://wiki.documentfoundation.org/Documentation/HowTos/Calc:ZTESTfunction" name="wiki.documentfoundation.org Documentation/HowTo/Calc/ZTEST function">Wiki page</link>.
<bookmarkvalue>Z.TEST function</bookmarkvalue>
Z.TEST
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZTESTMS">Calculates the probability of observing a z-statistic greater than the one computed based on a sample.</ahelp>
Z.TEST(Data; mu [; Sigma])
<item type="input">=Z.TEST(A2:A20; 9; 2)</item> returns the result of a z-test on a sample A2:A20 drawn from a population with known mean 9 and known standard deviation 2.
