<variable id="funcimcompnumb">A <emph>complex number</emph> is a string expression resulting in the form "a+bi" or "a+bj", where a and b are numbers.</variable>
<variable id="funcimrealnumb">If the <emph>complex number</emph> is actually a real number (b=0), then it can be either a string expression or a number value.</variable>
<variable id="funcimreturntext">The function always returns a string representing a complex number.</variable>
<variable id="funcimignorzero">If the result is a complex number with one of its parts (a or b) equal to zero, that part is not displayed.</variable>
<variable id="funcimagzero">The imaginary part is equal to zero, so it is not displayed in the result.</variable>
The result is presented in the string format and has the character "i" or "j" as an imaginary unit.
<variable id="string2551">String 1 [; String 2 [; …  [; String 255]]]</variable>
<emph>String 1, String 2, … , String 255</emph> are strings, references to cells or to cell ranges of strings.
<variable id="integer2551">Integer 1 [; Integer 2 [; … [; Integer 255]]]</variable>
<emph>Integer 1, Integer 2, … , Integer 255</emph> are integers, references to cells or to cell ranges of integers.
<variable id="number2541">Number 1 [; Number 2 [; … [; Number 254]]]</variable>
<emph>Number 1, Number 2, … , Number 254</emph> are numbers, references to cells or to cell ranges of numbers.
<variable id="number2551">Number 1 [; Number 2 [; … [; Number 255]]]</variable>
<emph>Number 1, Number 2, … , Number 255</emph> are numbers, references to cells or to cell ranges of numbers.
<variable id="logical2551">Logical 1 [; Logical 2 [; … [; Logical 255]]]</variable>
<emph>Logical 1, Logical 2,  … , Logical 255</emph> are boolean values, references to cells or to cell ranges of logical values.
<variable id="complex2551">Complex 1 [; Complex 2 [; … [; Complex 255]]]</variable>
<emph>Complex 1, Complex 2, … ,Complex 255</emph> are complex numbers, references to cells or to cell ranges of complex numbers. Complex numbers are entered in the form "x+yi" or "x+yj".
<variable id="reference2551">Reference 1 [; Reference 2 [; … [; Reference 255]]]</variable>
<emph>Reference 1, Reference 2, … ,Reference 255</emph> are references to cells.
This function is always recalculated whenever a recalculation occurs.
AGGREGATE function
<bookmarkvalue>AGGREGATE function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="aggregatehead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcaggregate.xhp">AGGREGATE</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="aggregatedes">This function returns an aggregate result of the calculations in the range. You can use different aggregate functions listed below. The Aggregate function enables you to omit hidden rows, errors, SUBTOTAL and other AGGREGATE function results in the calculation.</variable></ahelp>
AGGREGATE function is applied to vertical ranges of data with activated AutoFilter. If AutoFilter is not activated, automatic recalculation of the function result does not work for newly hidden rows. It is not supposed to work with horizontal ranges, however it can be applied to them as well, but with limitations. In particular, the AGGREGATE function applied to a horizontal data range does not recognize hiding columns, however correctly omits errors and results of SUBTOTAL and other AGGREGATE functions embedded into the row.
AGGREGATE(Function; Option; Number 1[; Number 2][; ... ;[Number 253]])
AGGREGATE(Function; Option; Array[; k])
<emph>Function</emph> – obligatory argument. A function index or a reference to a cell with value from 1 to 19, in accordance with the following table.
Function applied
<emph>Option</emph> – obligatory argument. An option index or reference to a cell with value from 0 to 7 determines what to ignore in the range for the function.
Option index
Option applied
Ignore only nested SUBTOTAL and AGGREGATE functions
Ignore only hidden rows, nested SUBTOTAL and AGGREGATE functions
Ignore only errors, nested SUBTOTAL and AGGREGATE functions
Ignore hidden rows, errors, nested SUBTOTAL and AGGREGATE functions
Ignore nothing
Ignore only hidden rows
Ignore only errors
Ignore only hidden rows and errors
<emph>Number1</emph> – required argument. The first numeric argument (if the range is set by a list of values inside the function) or a reference to a cell that contains it.
<emph>Number2, 3, ...</emph> – optional. A numeric argument or a reference to a cell (up to 253 arguments), for which you need the aggregate value.
<emph>Array</emph> – required argument. The array can be specified by the boundaries of the range, the name of the named range or the column label.
For using column labels “Automatically find columns and rows labels” function needs to be enabled.
<emph>k</emph> – required argument for the following functions: LARGE, SMALL, PERCENTILE.INC, QUARTILE.INC, PERCENTILE.EXC, QUARTILE.EXC. It is a numeric argument, which must correspond to the second argument of these functions.
<emph>ColumnOne</emph>
<emph>ColumnTwo</emph>
<emph>ColumnThree</emph>
#DIV/0!
<item type="input">=AGGREGATE(4;2;A2:A9)</item><br/>Returns maximum value for the range A2:A9 = 34, whereas <item type="input">=MAX(A2:A9)</item> returns the error Err:511.
<item type="input">=AGGREGATE(9;5;A5:C5)</item><br/>Returns sum for the range A5:C5 = 29, even if some of the columns are hidden.
<item type="input">=AGGREGATE(9;5;B2:B9)</item><br/>Returns sum of the column B = 115. If any row is hidden, the function omit its value, for example if the 7th row is hidden, the function returns 95.
If you need to apply the function with a 3D range, this example shows how to do it.
<item type="input">=AGGREGATE(13;3;Sheet1.B2:B9:Sheet3.B2:B9)</item><br/>The function returns mode of the values of second columns through sheets 1:3 (that have the same data) = 8.
You can use reference to a cell or a range for every argument in the formula. The following example shows how it works. Besides, it shows that you can use column labels to specify an array.
<item type="input">=AGGREGATE(E3;E5;'ColumnOne')</item><br/>If E3 = 13 and E5 = 5, the function returns mode of the first column = 10.
<link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#average">AVERAGE</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060181.xhp#count">COUNT</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060181.xhp#counta">COUNTA</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#max">MAX</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#min">MIN</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060106.xhp#Section26">PRODUCT</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060185.xhp#stdevdots">STDEV.S</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060185.xhp#stdevdotp">STDEV.P</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060106.xhp#Section16">SUM</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060185.xhp#vardots">VAR.S</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060185.xhp#vardotp">VAR.P</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#median">MEDIAN</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#modedotsngl">MODE.SNGL</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060183.xhp#large">LARGE</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060183.xhp#small">SMALL</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#percentileinc">PERCENTILE.INC</link> , <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#quartileinc">QUARTILE.INC</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#percentileexc">PERCENTILE.EXC</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060184.xhp#quartileexc">QUARTILE.EXC</link>
<link href="text/shared/optionen/01060500.xhp#hdid3156199">Automatically find column and row labels</link>
AVERAGEIF function
<bookmarkvalue>AVERAGEIF function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>arithmetic mean;satisfying condition</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="averageifhead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcaverageif.xhp">AVERAGEIF</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="averageifdes">Returns the arithmetic mean of all cells in a range that satisfy a given condition. The AVERAGEIF function sums up all the results that match the logical test and divides this sum by the quantity of selected values.</variable></ahelp>
AVERAGEIF(Range; Criterion [; AverageRange ])
<emph>Range</emph> – required argument. An array, a name of named range or a label of a column or a row containing numbers for averaging or numbers or text for the condition.
<emph>Criterion</emph> – required argument. A condition in the form of expression or a cell reference with expression that defines what cells should be used to calculate the mean. The expression can contain text, numbers, regular expressions (if enabled in calculation options) or wildcards (if enabled in calculation options).
<emph>AverageRange</emph> – optional. It is a range of values for calculating the mean.
If the <emph>AverageRange</emph> is not specified, <emph>Range</emph> is used for both, the calculation of the mean and the search according to the condition. If  <emph>AverageRange</emph> is specified, the <emph>Range</emph> is used only for the condition test, while <emph>AverageRange</emph> is used for the average calculation.
If a cell in a range of values for calculating the mean is empty or contains text, function AVERAGEIF ignores this cell.<br/>If the whole range is empty, contains only text or all values of the range do not satisfy the condition (or any combination of those), the function returns the #DIV/0! error.
Simple usage
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(B2:B6;"<35")</item>
Calculates the average for values of the range B2:B6 that are less than 35. Returns 19, because the second row does not participate in the calculation.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the average for values of the same range that are less than the maximum value of this range. Returns 19, because the largest value (the second row) does not participate in the calculation.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(B2:B6;">"SMALL(B2:B6;1))</item>
Calculates the average for values of the same range that are greater than the first smallest value of this range. Returns 25, because the first smallest value (the fourth row) does not participate in the calculation.
Using the AverageRange
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(B2:B6;"<35";C2:C6)</item>
The function searches what values are less than 35 in the B2:B6 range, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the C2:C6 range. Returns 145, because the second row does not participate in the calculation.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(B2:B6;">"MIN(B2:B6);C2:C6)</item>
The function searches what values from the range B2:B6 are greater than the least value in the B2:B6 range, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the C2:C6 range. Returns 113.3, because the fourth row (where there is the least value in the range B2:B6) does not participate in the calculation.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(B2:B6;"<"LARGE(B2:B6;2);C2:C6)</item>
The function searches what values from the range B2:B6 are less than the second large value in the B2:B6 range, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the C2:C6 range. Returns 180, because only the fourth row participates in the calculation.
Using regular expressions
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(A2:A6;"pen";B2:B6)</item>
The function searches what cells from the range A2:A6 contain only the word “pen”, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the B2:B6 range. Returns 35, because only the second row participates in the calculation. The search is performed in the A2:A6 range, but the values are returned from the B2:B6 range.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(A2:A6;"pen.*";B2:B6)</item>
The function searches what cells from the range A2:A6 begin with “pen” ending with any quantity of other characters, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the B2:B6 range. Returns 27.5, because now also “pencil” satisfies the condition, and both, first and second rows participate in the calculation.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(A2:A6;".*book.*";B2:B6)</item>
The function searches what cells from the range A2:A6 contain “book” starting and ending with any quantity of other characters, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the B2:B6 range. Returns 18.5, because only third and fourth rows participate in the calculation.
Reference to a cell as a criterion
If you need to change a criterion easily, you may want to specify it in a separate cell and use a reference to this cell in the condition of AVERAGEIF function.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(A2:A6;".*"E2".*";B2:B6)</item>
The function searches what cells from the range A2:A6 contain a combination of characters specified in E2 starting and ending with any quantity of other characters, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the B2:B6 range. If E2 = book, the function returns 18.5.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIF(B2:B6;"<"E2;C2:C6)</item>
The function searches what cells from the range B2:B6 are less than the value specified in E2, and calculates the average of corresponding values from the C2:C6 range. If E2 = 35, the function returns 145.
AVERAGEIFS function
<bookmarkvalue>AVERAGEIFS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>arithmetic mean;satisfying conditions</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="averageifshead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcaverageifs.xhp">AVERAGEIFS</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="averageifsdes">Returns the arithmetic mean of all cells in a range that satisfy given multiple criteria. The AVERAGEIFS function sums up all the results that match the logical tests and divides this sum by the quantity of selected values.</variable></ahelp>
AVERAGEIFS(<embedvar href="text/scalc/01/exdatastatfunc.xhp#args" markup="ignore"/>)
<emph>Funcrange</emph> – required argument. It is a range of cells, a name of a named range or a label of a column or a row containing values for calculating the mean.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIFS(B2:B6;B2:B6;">=20")</item>
Calculates the average for values of the range B2:B6 that are greater than or equal to 20. Returns 25, because the fifth row does not meet the criterion.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">=20";C2:C6;">70")</item>
Calculates the average for values of the range C2:C6 that are greater than 70 and correspond to cells of B2:B6 with values  greater than or equal to 20. Returns 137.5, because the second and fifth rows do not meet at least one criterion.
Using regular expressions and nested functions
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">"MIN(B2:B6);B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the average for values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all values of the range B2:B6 except its minimum and maximum. Returns 127.5, because the third and fifth rows do not meet at least one criterion.
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;"pen.*";B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the average for values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all cells of the A2:A6 range starting with "pen" and to all cells of the B2:B6 range except its maximum. Returns 65, because only second row meets all criteria.
If you need to change a criterion easily, you may want to specify it in a separate cell and use a reference to this cell in the condition of AVERAGEIFS function. For example, the above function can be rewritten as follows:
<item type="input">=AVERAGEIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;E2".*";B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
If E2 = pen, the function returns 65, because the link to the cell is substituted with its content.
Ceiling functions
<bookmarkvalue>CEILING function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>rounding;up to multiples of significance</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="CEILINGh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcceiling.xhp#ceiling" name="CEILING">CEILING</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCOBERGRENZE">Rounds a number to the nearest multiple of a significance value.</ahelp>
For a positive number and a positive significance value, the function rounds up (away from zero). For a negative number and a negative significance value, the direction of rounding is determined by the value of a mode parameter. The function returns an error if the number and significance values have opposite signs.
If the spreadsheet is exported to Microsoft Excel, the CEILING function is exported as the equivalent CEILING.MATH function that has existed since Excel 2013. If you plan to use the spreadsheet with earlier Excel versions, use either CEILING.PRECISE that has existed since Excel 2010, or CEILING.XCL that is exported as the CEILING function compatible with all Excel versions.
CEILING(Number [; Significance [; Mode]])
<emph>Number</emph> is the number that is to be rounded, or a reference to a cell containing the number.
<emph>Significance</emph> (optional) is the value, or a reference to a cell containing the value, to whose multiple <emph>Number</emph> is to be rounded. It defaults to +1 or -1 depending on the sign of <emph>Number</emph>.
<emph>Mode</emph> (optional) is a number, or a reference to a cell containing a number. The function only uses <emph>Mode</emph> if both <emph>Number</emph> and <emph>Significance</emph> are negative. Then if <emph>Mode</emph> is given and not equal to zero, numbers are rounded down (away from zero); if <emph>Mode</emph> is equal to zero or not given, negative numbers are rounded up (towards zero).
<input>=CEILING(3.45)</input> returns 4.
<input>=CEILING(3.45; 3)</input> returns 6.
<input>=CEILING(-1.234)</input> returns -1.
<input>=CEILING(-45.67; -2; 0)</input> returns -44.
<input>=CEILING(-45.67; -2; 1)</input> returns -46.
<bookmarkvalue>CEILING.PRECISE function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>rounding;up to multiples of significance</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="CEILING.PRECISEh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcceiling.xhp#ceilingprecise" name="CEILING.PRECISE">CEILING.PRECISE</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCEILMS">Rounds a number up to the nearest multiple of a significance value.</ahelp>
For a positive number the function rounds up (away from zero). For a negative number, the function rounds up (towards zero). The sign of the significance value is ignored.
This function calculates identical results to the <link href="#Section312" name="isoceiling">ISO.CEILING</link> function.
CEILING.PRECISE(Number [; Significance])
<emph>Significance</emph> (optional) is the value, or a reference to a cell containing the value, to whose multiple <emph>Number</emph> is to be rounded. It defaults to 1.
<input>=CEILING.PRECISE(3.45)</input> returns 4.
<input>=CEILING.PRECISE(-45.67; 2)</input> returns -44.
<bookmarkvalue>CEILING.MATH function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="CEILING.MATHh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcceiling.xhp#ceilingmath" name="CEILING.MATH">CEILING.MATH</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCEILMATH">Rounds a number to the nearest multiple of a significance value.</ahelp>
For a positive number the function rounds up (away from zero). For a negative number, the direction of rounding is determined by the value of a mode parameter. The sign of the significance value is ignored.
This function exists for interoperability with Microsoft Excel 2013 or newer.
CEILING.MATH(Number [; Significance [; Mode]])
<emph>Mode</emph> (optional) is a number, or a reference to a cell containing a number. If <emph>Mode</emph> is given and not equal to zero, a negative <emph>Number</emph> is rounded down (away from zero). If <emph>Mode</emph> is equal to zero or is not given, a negative <emph>Number</emph> is rounded up (towards zero).
<input>=CEILING.MATH(3.45)</input> returns 4.
<input>=CEILING.MATH(3.45; -3)</input> returns 6.
<input>=CEILING.MATH(-1.234)</input> returns -1.
<input>=CEILING.MATH(-45.67; -2; 0)</input> returns -44.
<input>=CEILING.MATH(-45.67; +2; 1)</input> returns -46.
<bookmarkvalue>CEILING.XCL function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="CEILING.XCLh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcceiling.xhp#ceilingxcl" name="CEILING.XCL">CEILING.XCL</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCEILMS">Rounds a number to the nearest multiple of a significance value.</ahelp>
For a positive number and a positive significance value, the function rounds up (away from zero). For a negative number and a positive significance value, the function rounds up (towards zero). For a negative number and a negative significance value, the function rounds down (away from zero). The function returns an error if the number is positive and the significance value is negative.
This function exists for interoperability with Microsoft Excel 2007 or older. If a Calc spreadsheet is exported to Microsoft Excel, references to Calc’s CEILING.XCL function are exported as references to Excel’s CEILING function, which is compatible with all Excel versions. If a Microsoft Excel spreadsheet is imported into Calc, references to Excel’s CEILING function are imported as references to Calc’s CEILING.XCL function.
CEILING.XCL(Number; Significance)
<emph>Significance</emph> is the value, or a reference to a cell containing the value, to whose multiple <emph>Number</emph> is to be rounded.
<input>=CEILING.XCL(3.45,2)</input> returns 4.
<input>=CEILING.XCL(-45.67; 2)</input> returns -44.
<input>=CEILING.XCL(-45.67; -2)</input> returns -46.
<bookmarkvalue>ISO.CEILING function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>rounding;up to multiples of significance</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="ISO.CEILINGh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcceiling.xhp#isoceiling" name="ISO.CEILING">ISO.CEILING</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCCEILISO">Rounds a number up to the nearest multiple of a significance value.</ahelp>
This function calculates identical results to the <link href="#Section311" name="ceilingprecise">CEILING.PRECISE</link> function.
ISO.CEILING(Number [; Significance])
<input>=ISO.CEILING(3.45)</input> returns 4.
<input>=ISO.CEILING(-45.67; 2)</input> returns -44.
COLOR function
<bookmarkvalue>colors;numerical values</bookmarkvalue>         <bookmarkvalue>colors;calculating in spreadsheets</bookmarkvalue>         <bookmarkvalue>COLOR function</bookmarkvalue>
<ahelp hid=".">Return a numeric value calculated by a combination of three colors (red, green and blue) and the alpha channel, in the RGBA color system.</ahelp> The result depends on the color system used by your computer.
COLOR(Red; Green; Blue [; Alpha])
<emph>Red, Green and Blue</emph> – required arguments. The value for the red, green and blue components of the color. The values must be between 0 and 255. Zero means no color component and 255 means full color component.
<emph>Alpha</emph> – optional argument. The value for the alpha channel or alpha composite. Alpha is a integer value between 0 and 255. The value of zero for alpha means the color is fully transparent, whereas a value of 255 in the alpha channel gives a fully opaque color.
<item type="input">COLOR(255;255;255;1)</item> returns 33554431
<item type="input">COLOR(0;0;255;0)</item> returns 255
<item type="input">COLOR(0;0;255;255)</item> returns 4278190335
<item type="input">COLOR(0;0;400;0)</item> returns Err:502 (Invalid argument) because the blue value is greater than 255.
CONCAT function
<bookmarkvalue>CONCAT function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="concatfunct"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcconcat.xhp" name="concat">CONCAT</link></variable>
<variable id="concatfunction"><ahelp hid=".">Concatenates one or more strings</ahelp></variable>
CONCAT is an enhancement of CONCATENATE, as CONCAT also accepts ranges as arguments, like B2:E5, K:K or K:M.
When ranges are used, the cells are traversed row by row (from top to bottom) to concatenate.
CONCAT( <embedvar href="text/scalc/01/fulfunc.xhp#string2551" markup="keep"/> )
<input>=CONCAT("Hello ", A1:C3)</input>  concatenates the string "Hello" with all strings in range <literal>A1:C3</literal>.
<link href="text/scalc/01/04060110.xhp#concatenate" name="concatenate">CONCATENATE</link>
COUNTIFS function
<bookmarkvalue>COUNTIFS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>counting row;satisfying criteria</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>counting column;satisfying criteria</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="countifshead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funccountifs.xhp">COUNTIFS</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="countifsdes">Returns the count of cells that meet criteria in multiple ranges.</variable></ahelp>
COUNTIFS(Range1; Criterion1[; Range2; Criterion2][; ... ; [Range127; Criterion127]])
<emph>Range1, Range2, ...</emph> and <emph>Criterion1, Criterion2, ...</emph> must have the same size, otherwise the function returns err:502 - Invalid argument.
<item type="input">=COUNTIFS(B2:B6;">=20")</item>
Counts the amount of rows of the range B2:B6 with values greater than or equal to 20. Returns 3, because the fifth and the sixth rows do not meet the criterion.
<item type="input">=COUNTIFS(B2:B6;">=20";C2:C6;">70")</item>
Counts the amount of rows that contain simultaneously values greater than 70 in the C2:C6 range and values greater than or equal to 20 in the B2:B6 range. Returns 2, because the second, the fifth and the sixth rows do not meet at least one criterion.
For these examples to work as described, make sure that <emph>Enable regular expressions in formulas</emph> is selected in <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><menuitem>%PRODUCTNAME - Preferences</menuitem></caseinline><defaultinline><menuitem>Tools - Options</menuitem></defaultinline></switchinline><menuitem> - $[officename] Calc - Calculate</menuitem>.
<item type="input">=COUNTIFS(B2:B6;"[:alpha:]*")</item>
Counts the amount of rows of the B2:B6 range that contain only alphabet symbols. Returns 1, because only sixth row meets the criterion.
<item type="input">=COUNTIFS(B2:B6;">"MIN(B2:B6);B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Counts the amount of rows of the B2:B6 range excluding rows with minimum and maximum values of this range. Returns 2, because the third, the fifth and the sixth rows do not meet at least one criterion.
<item type="input">=COUNTIFS(A2:A6;"pen.*";B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Counts the amount of rows that correspond to all cells of the A2:A6 range starting with "pen" and to all cells of the B2:B6 range with exception of its maximum. Returns 1, because only second row meets all criteria.
If you need to change a criterion easily, you may want to specify it in a separate cell and use a reference to this cell in the condition of the COUNTIFS function. For example, the above function can be rewritten as follows:
<item type="input">=COUNTIFS(A2:A6;E2".*";B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
If E2 = pen, the function returns 1, because the link to the cell is substituted with its content and it works as a function above.
DATE
<bookmarkvalue>DATE function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="date"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcdate.xhp">DATE</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCDATUM">This function calculates a date specified by year, month, day and displays it in the cell's formatting.</ahelp> The default format of a cell containing the DATE function is the date format, but you can format the cells with any other number format.
DATE(Year; Month; Day)
<emph>Year</emph> is an integer between 1583 and 9957 or between 0 and 99.
In <switchinline select="sys"><caseinline select="MAC"><item type="menuitem">%PRODUCTNAME - Preferences</item></caseinline><defaultinline><item type="menuitem">Tools - Options</item></defaultinline></switchinline><item type="menuitem"> - $[officename] - General </item>you can set from which year a two-digit number entry is recognized as 20xx.
<emph>Month</emph> is an integer indicating the month.
<emph>Day</emph> is an integer indicating the day of the month.
If the values for month and day are out of bounds, they are carried over to the next digit. If you enter <item type="input">=DATE(00;12;31)</item> the result will be 2000-12-31. If, on the other hand, you enter <item type="input">=DATE(00;13;31)</item> the result will be 2001-01-31.
<item type="input">=DATE(00;1;31)</item> yields 1/31/00 if the cell format setting is MM/DD/YY.
DATEDIF
<bookmarkvalue>DATEDIF function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="datedif"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcdatedif.xhp">DATEDIF</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCDATEDIF">This function returns the number of whole days, months or years between Start date and End date.</ahelp>
DATEDIF(Start date; End date; Interval)
<emph>Start date</emph> is the date from when the calculation is carried out.
<emph>End date</emph> is the date until the calculation is carried out. End date must be later, than Start date.
<emph>Interval</emph> is a string, accepted values are "d", "m", "y", "ym", "md" or "yd".
Value for "Interval"
Number of whole days between Start date and End date.
Number of whole months between Start date and End date.
Number of whole years between Start date and End date.
Number of whole months when subtracting years from the difference of Start date and End date.
Number of whole days when subtracting years and months from the difference of Start date and End date.
Number of whole days when subtracting years from the difference of Start date and End date.
Birthday calculation. A man was born on 1974-04-17. Today is 2012-06-13.
<item type="input">=DATEDIF("1974-04-17";"2012-06-13";"y")</item> yields 38.
<item type="input">=DATEDIF("1974-04-17";"2012-06-13";"ym")</item> yields 1.
<item type="input">=DATEDIF("1974-04-17";"2012-06-13";"md")</item> yields 27.
So he is 38 years, 1 month and 27 days old.
<item type="input">=DATEDIF(DATE(1974,4,17);"2012-06-13";"m")</item> yields 457, he has been living for 457 months.
<item type="input">=DATEDIF("1974-04-17";"2012-06-13";"d")</item> yields 13937, he has been living for 13937 days.
<item type="input">=DATEDIF("1974-04-17";DATE(2012;06;13);"yd")</item> yields 57, his birthday was 57 days ago.
DATEVALUE
<bookmarkvalue>DATEVALUE function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="datevalue"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcdatevalue.xhp">DATEVALUE</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCDATWERT">Returns the internal date number for text in quotes.</ahelp>
The internal date number is returned as a number. The number is determined by the date system that is used by $[officename] to calculate dates.
If the text string also includes a time value, DATEVALUE only returns the integer part of the conversion.
DATEVALUE("Text")
<emph>Text</emph> is a valid date expression and must be entered with quotation marks.
<item type="input">=DATEVALUE("1954-07-20")</item>  yields 19925.
DAY
<bookmarkvalue>DAY function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="day"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcday.xhp">DAY</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCTAG">Returns the day of given date value.</ahelp> The day is returned as an integer between 1 and 31. You can also enter a negative date/time value.
DAY(Number)
<emph>Number</emph> is the internal date number.
<item type="input">=DAY(1)</item>  returns 31 (since $[officename] starts counting at zero from December 30, 1899)
<item type="input">=DAY(NOW())</item>  returns the current day.
<item type="input">=DAY(C4)</item>  returns 5 if you enter 1901-08-05 in cell C4 (the date value might get formatted differently after you press Enter).
DAYS
<bookmarkvalue>DAYS function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="days"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcdays.xhp">DAYS</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCTAGE">Calculates the difference between two date values.</ahelp> The result returns the number of days between the two days.
DAYS(Date2; Date1)
<emph>Date1</emph> is the start date, <emph>Date2</emph> is the end date. If <emph>Date2</emph> is an earlier date than <emph>Date1</emph> the result is a negative number.
<item type="input">=DAYS(NOW();"2010-01-01"))</item> returns the number of days from January 1, 2010 until today.
<item type="input">=DAYS("1990-10-10";"1980-10-10")</item>  returns 3652 days.
DAYS360
<bookmarkvalue>DAYS360 function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="days360"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcdays360.xhp">DAYS360</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCTAGE360">Returns the difference between two dates based on the 360 day year used in interest calculations.</ahelp>
DAYS360(Date1; Date2[; Type])
If <emph>Date2</emph> is earlier than <emph>Date1</emph>, the function will return a negative number.
The optional argument <emph>Type</emph> determines the type of difference calculation. If Type = 0 or if the argument is missing, the US method (NASD, National Association of Securities Dealers) is used. If Type <> 0, the European method is used.
<item type="input">=DAYS360("2000-01-01";NOW())</item> returns the number of interest days from January 1, 2000 until today.
EASTERSUNDAY
<bookmarkvalue>EASTERSUNDAY function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="eastersunday"><link href="text/scalc/01/funceastersunday.xhp">EASTERSUNDAY</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCOSTERSONNTAG">Returns the date of Easter Sunday for the entered year.</ahelp>
EASTERSUNDAY(Year)
<emph>Year</emph> is an integer between 1583 and 9956 or 0 and 99. You can also calculate other holidays by simple addition with this date.
Easter Monday = EASTERSUNDAY(Year) + 1
Good Friday = EASTERSUNDAY(Year) - 2
Pentecost Sunday = EASTERSUNDAY(Year) + 49
Pentecost Monday = EASTERSUNDAY(Year) + 50
<item type="input">=EASTERSUNDAY(2000)</item>  returns 2000-04-23.
<item type="input">=EASTERSUNDAY(2000)+49</item>  returns the internal serial number 36688. The result is 2000-06-11. Format the serial date number as a date, for example in the format YYYY-MM-DD.
EDATE
<bookmarkvalue>EDATE function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="edate"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcedate.xhp">EDATE</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCEDATE">The result is a date which is a number of <emph>months</emph> away from the <emph>start date</emph>. Only months are considered; days are not used for calculation.</ahelp>
EDATE(StartDate; Months)
<emph>StartDate</emph> is a date.
<emph>Months</emph> is the number of months before (negative) or after (positive) the start date.
What date is one month prior to 2001-03-31?
<item type="input">=EDATE("2001-03-31";-1)</item> returns the serial number 36950. Formatted as a date, this is 2001-02-28.
EOMONTH
<bookmarkvalue>EOMONTH function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="eomonth"><link href="text/scalc/01/funceomonth.xhp">EOMONTH</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCEOMONTH">Returns the date of the last day of a month which falls months away from the start date.</ahelp>
EOMONTH(StartDate; Months)
<emph>StartDate</emph> is a date (the starting point of the calculation).
What is the last day of the month that falls 6 months after September 14 2001?
<item type="input">=EOMONTH(DATE(2001;9;14);6)</item> returns the serial number 37346. Formatted as a date, this is 2002-03-31.
<item type="input">=EOMONTH("2001-09-14";6)</item> works as well. If the date is given as string, it has to be in ISO format.
ERROR.TYPE function
<bookmarkvalue>ERROR.TYPE function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>index of the Error type</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="errortypehead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcerrortype.xhp">ERROR.TYPE</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="errortypedes">Returns a number representing a specific Error type, or the error value #N/A, if there is no error. </variable></ahelp>
ERROR.TYPE(Errorvalue)
<emph>Errorvalue</emph> – required argument. The error value or a reference to a cell, whose value needs to be processed.
Error value
Returns
Err:511
#REF!
#NAME?
#NUM!
#N/A
Anything else
<item type="input">=ERROR.TYPE(#N/A)</item>
Returns 7, because 7 is the index number of the error value #N/A.
<item type="input">=ERROR.TYPE(A3)</item>
If A3 contains an expression equivalent to the division by zero, the function returns 2, because 2 is the index number of the error value #DIV/0!
More advanced way
If in division A1 by A2, A2 can turn to zero, you can handle the situation as follows:
<item type="input">=IF(ISERROR(A1/A2);IF(ERROR.TYPE(A1/A2)=2;"the denominator can't be equal to zero");A1/A2)</item>
The ISERROR function returns TRUE or FALSE depending on whether there is an error or not. If the error takes place, the function IF addresses to the second argument, if there is no error, it returns the result of the division. The second argument checks the index number representing the specific Error type, and if it is equal to 2, it returns the specified text "the denominator can't be zero" or 0 otherwise. Thus, clear text would signify the division by zero, the result of the division would appear when the division is successful, or if there is, for example, an error of another type, zero would be returned.
If the ERROR.TYPE function is used as condition of the IF function and the ERROR.TYPE returns #N/A, the IF function returns #N/A as well. Use ISERROR to avoid it as shown in the example above.
<link href="text/scalc/01/04060104.xhp#iserror">ISERROR</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060104.xhp#na">NA</link>, <link href="text/scalc/01/04060104.xhp#Section4">IF</link>
<link href="text/scalc/05/02140000.xhp" name="Error codes">Error codes</link>
FINDB Function
<bookmarkvalue>FINDB Function</bookmarkvalue>            <bookmarkvalue>find text;FINDB Function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="findb"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcfindb.xhp" name="findb">FINDB</link></variable>
<variable id="variable name"><ahelp hid=".">Returns the starting position of a given text, using byte positions. FINDB is case sensitive.</ahelp></variable>
FINDB(Find Text ; Text [; Position])
<emph>Find Text</emph>: The text or text expression to be found.
<emph>Text</emph>: the text in which the search is to be made.
<emph>Position</emph>: The position in the text where the search starts.
<input>=FINDB("ᄫᄬ";"ᄩᄔᄕᄜᄝᄞᄠgᄢᄣᄫᄬᄭᄮᄯᄲᄶ";17)</input> returns 19.
FLOOR Functions
<bookmarkvalue>FLOOR function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>rounding;down to nearest multiple of significance</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="FLOORh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcfloor.xhp#floor" name="FLOOR">FLOOR</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCUNTERGRENZE">Rounds a number to the nearest multiple of a significance value.</ahelp>
For a positive number and a positive significance value, the function rounds down (towards zero). For a negative number and a negative significance value, the direction of rounding is determined by the value of a mode parameter. The function returns an error if the number and significance values have opposite signs.
If the spreadsheet is exported to Microsoft Excel, the FLOOR function is exported as the equivalent FLOOR.MATH function that has existed since Excel 2013. If you plan to use the spreadsheet with earlier Excel versions, use either FLOOR.PRECISE that has existed since Excel 2010, or FLOOR.XCL that is exported as the FLOOR function compatible with all Excel versions.
FLOOR(Number[; Significance[; Mode]])
<emph>Mode</emph> (optional) is a number, or a reference to a cell containing a number. The function only uses <emph>Mode</emph> if both <emph>Number</emph> and <emph>Significance</emph> are negative. Then if <emph>Mode</emph> is given and not equal to zero, numbers are rounded up (towards zero); if <emph>Mode</emph> is equal to zero or not given, negative numbers are rounded down (away from zero).
<input>=FLOOR(3.45)</input> returns 3.
<input>=FLOOR(3.45, 3)</input> returns 3.
<input>=FLOOR(-1.234)</input> returns -2.
<input>=FLOOR(-45.67, -2, 0)</input> returns -46.
<input>=FLOOR(-45.67, -2, 1)</input> returns -44.
<bookmarkvalue>FLOOR.MATH function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="FLOOR.MATHh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcfloor.xhp#floormath" name="FLOOR.MATH">FLOOR.MATH</link></variable>
Rounds a number to the nearest multiple of a significance value.
For a positive number the function rounds down (towards zero). For a negative number, the direction of rounding is determined by the value of a mode parameter. The sign of the significance value is ignored.
FLOOR.MATH(Number[; Significance[; Mode]])
<emph>Mode</emph> (optional) is a number, or a reference to a cell containing a number. If <emph>Mode</emph> is given and not equal to zero, a negative <emph>Number</emph> is rounded up (towards zero). If <emph>Mode</emph> is equal to zero or is not given, a negative <emph>Number</emph> is rounded down (away from zero).
<input>=FLOOR.MATH(3.45)</input> returns 3.
<input>=FLOOR.MATH(3.45,-3)</input> returns 3.
<input>=FLOOR.MATH(-1.234)</input> returns -2.
<input>=FLOOR.MATH(-45.67,-2, 0)</input> returns -46.
<input>=FLOOR.MATH(-45.67,+2, 1)</input> returns -44.
<bookmarkvalue>FLOOR.PRECISE function</bookmarkvalue><bookmarkvalue>rounding;down to nearest multiple of significance</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="FLOOR.PRECISEh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcfloor.xhp#floorprecise" name="FLOOR.PRECISE">FLOOR.PRECISE</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCFLOORMS">Rounds a number down to the nearest multiple of a significance value.</ahelp>
For a positive number the function rounds down (towards zero). For a negative number, the function rounds down (away form zero). The sign of the significance value is ignored.
FLOOR.PRECISE(Number[; Significance])
<input>=FLOOR.PRECISE(3.45)</input> returns 3.
<input>=FLOOR.PRECISE(-45.67,2)</input> returns -46.
<bookmarkvalue>FLOOR.XCL function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="FLOOR.XCLh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcfloor.xhp#floorxcl" name="FLOOR.XCL">FLOOR.XCL</link></variable>
For a positive number and a positive significance value, the function rounds down (towards zero). For a negative number and a positive significance value, the function rounds down (away from zero). For a negative number and a negative significance value, the function rounds up (towards zero). The function returns an error if the number is positive and the significance value is negative.
This function exists for interoperability with Microsoft Excel 2007 or older. If a Calc spreadsheet is exported to Microsoft Excel, references to Calc’s FLOOR.XCL function are exported as references to Excel’s FLOOR function, which is compatible with all Excel versions. If a Microsoft Excel spreadsheet is imported into Calc, references to Excel’s FLOOR function are imported as references to Calc’s FLOOR.XCL function.
FLOOR.XCL(Number; Significance)
<input>=FLOOR.XCL(3.45,2)</input> returns 2.
<input>=FLOOR.XCL(-45.67,2)</input> returns -46.
<input>=FLOOR.XCL(-45.67,-2)</input> returns -44.

<bookmarkvalue>FORECAST.ETS.ADD function</bookmarkvalue>

FORECAST.ETS.ADD calculates with the model
FORECAST.ETS.ADD(targets, values, timeline, [periodlength], [datacompletion], [aggregation])
=FORECAST.ETS.ADD(DATE(2014;1;1);Values;Timeline;1;TRUE();1)
Returns 157.166666666667, the additive forecast for January 2014 based on <emph>Values</emph> and <emph>Timeline</emph> named ranges above, with one sample per period, no missing data, and AVERAGE as aggregation.

FORECAST.ETS.PI.ADD
<bookmarkvalue>FORECAST.ETS.PI.ADD function</bookmarkvalue>
<link href="text/scalc/01/funcforecastetspiadd.xhp">FORECAST.ETS.PI.ADD function</link>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCFORECASTETSPIA">Calculates the prediction interval(s) for additive forecast based on the historical data using ETS or EDS algorithms.</ahelp> EDS is used when argument <emph>periodlength</emph> is 0, otherwise ETS is used.
FORECAST.ETS.PI.ADD calculates with the model
FORECAST.ETS.PI.ADD(target, values, timeline, [confidencelevel], [periodlength], [datacompletion], [aggregation])
For example, with a 90% Confidence level, a 90% prediction interval will be computed (90% of future points are to fall within this radius from forecast).
Note on prediction intervals: there is no exact mathematical way to calculate this for forecasts, there are various approximations. Prediction intervals tend to be increasingly 'over-optimistic' when increasing distance of the forecast-X from the observation data set.
For ETS, Calc uses an approximation based on 1000 calculations with random variations within the standard deviation of the observation data set (the historical values).
=FORECAST.ETS.PI.ADD(DATE(2014;1;1);Values;Timeline;0.9;1;TRUE();1)
Returns 18.8061295551355, the prediction interval for additive forecast for January 2014 based on <emph>Values</emph> and <emph>Timeline</emph> named ranges above, 90% (=0.9) confidence level, with one sample per period, no missing data, and AVERAGE as aggregation.
=FORECAST.ETS.PI.ADD(DATE(2014;1;1);Values;Timeline;0.8;4;TRUE();7)
Returns 23.4416821953741, the prediction interval for additive forecast for January 2014 based on <emph>Values</emph> and <emph>Timeline</emph> named ranges above, with confidence level of 0.8, period length of 4, no missing data, and SUM as aggregation.
See also:  <link href="text/scalc/01/funcforecastetsadd.xhp">FORECAST.ETS.ADD</link>,  <link href="text/scalc/01/funcforecastetsmult.xhp">FORECAST.ETS.MULT</link>,  <link href="text/scalc/01/funcforecastetsstatadd.xhp">FORECAST.ETS.STAT.ADD</link>,  <link href="text/scalc/01/funcforecastetsstatmult.xhp">FORECAST.ETS.STAT.MULT</link>,  <link href="text/scalc/01/funcforecastetspimult.xhp">FORECAST.ETS.PI.MULT</link>  <link href="text/scalc/01/funcforecastetsseason.xhp">FORECAST.ETS.SEASONALITY</link>,  <link href="text/scalc/01/04060185.xhp#forecast">FORECAST</link>,  <link href="text/scalc/01/04060185.xhp#forecastlinear">FORECAST.LINEAR</link>

FOURIER function
<bookmarkvalue>FOURIER function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="fourierfunct"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcfourier.xhp" name="fourierfunction">FOURIER</link></variable>
<variable id="textjoinfunction"><ahelp hid=".">Computes the  Discrete Fourier Transform [DFT] of an input array of complex numbers using a couple of Fast Fourier Transform (FFT) algorithms.</ahelp></variable> The  function is an <link href="text/scalc/01/04060107.xhp" name="array formula">array formula</link>.
FOURIER(Array; GroupedByColumns [; Inverse [; Polar [; MinimumMagnitude]]])
<emph>Array</emph> is a 2 x N or N x 2 range representing an array of complex number to be transformed, where N is the length of the array. The array represents the real and imaginary parts of the data.
<emph>GroupedByColumns</emph> is a logical (TRUE or FALSE, 1 or 0) argument. When TRUE the array is grouped by columns where the first column contains the real part of the complex number and the second columns contains the imaginary part of the complex number. When FALSE, the first row contains the real part of the complex number and the second row contains the imaginary part of the complex number. If there is only 1 column (row), the input sequence is treated as purely real.
<emph>Inverse</emph> is an optional logical (TRUE or FALSE, 1 or 0) argument. When TRUE, calculates the inverse Discrete Fourier Transform. The default value is FALSE.
<emph>Polar</emph>: is an optional logical (TRUE or FALSE, 1 or 0) argument. Indicates whether the final output is in polar coordinates (magnitude, phase). This argument is optional and the default value is FALSE.
<emph>MinimumMagnitude</emph>: used only if Polar=TRUE. All frequency components with magnitude less than <emph>MinimumMagnitude</emph> will be suppressed with a zero magnitude-phase entry. This is very useful when looking at the magnitude-phase spectrum of a signal because there is always some very tiny amount of rounding error when doing FFT algorithms and results in incorrect non-zero phase for non-existent frequencies. By providing a suitable value to this parameter, these non-existent frequency components can be suppressed. By default the value of <emph>MinimumMagnitude</emph> is 0.0, and no suppression is done by default.
HOUR
<bookmarkvalue>HOUR function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="hour"><link href="text/scalc/01/funchour.xhp">HOUR</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCSTUNDE">Returns the hour for a given time value.</ahelp> The hour is returned as an integer between 0 and 23.
HOUR(Number)
<emph>Number</emph>, as a time value, is a decimal, for which the hour is to be returned.
<item type="input">=HOUR(NOW())</item> returns the current hour
<item type="input">=HOUR(C4)</item> returns 17 if the contents of C4 = <item type="input">17:20:00</item>.
IFS function
<bookmarkvalue>IFS function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="ifsfunct"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcifs.xhp" name="function ifs">IFS</link></variable>
<variable id="variable name"><ahelp hid=".">IFS is a multiple IF-function.</ahelp></variable>
IFS(expression1; result1[; expression2; result2][; ... ; [expression127; result127]])
<emph>expression1, expression2, ...</emph> are any boolean values or expressions that can be TRUE or FALSE
<emph>result1, result2, ... </emph> are the values that are returned if the logical test is TRUE
IFS( expression1, result1, expression2, result2, expression3, result3 ) is executed as
IF expression1 is TRUE
THEN result1
ELSE IF expression2 is TRUE
THEN result2
ELSE IF expression3 is TRUE
THEN result3
To get a default result should no expression be TRUE, add a last expression that is always TRUE, like TRUE or 1=1 followed by the default result.
If there is a result missing for an expression or is no expression is TRUE, a #N/A error is returned.
If expression is neither TRUE or FALSE, a #VALUE error is returned.
<link href="text/scalc/01/04060105.xhp#Section4" name="if">IF</link>

ISOWEEKNUM
<bookmarkvalue>ISOWEEKNUM function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="isoweeknum"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcisoweeknum.xhp">ISOWEEKNUM</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCISOWEEKNUM">ISOWEEKNUM calculates the week number of the year for the internal date value.</ahelp>
The International Standard ISO 8601 has decreed that Monday shall be the first day of the week. A week that lies partly in one year and partly in another is assigned a number in the year in which most of its days lie. That means that week number 1 of any year is the week that contains the January 4th.
ISOWEEKNUM(Number)
<item type="input">=ISOWEEKNUM(DATE(1995;1;1))</item>  returns 52. Week 1 starts on Monday, 1995-01-02.
<item type="input">=ISOWEEKNUM(DATE(1999;1;1))</item>  returns 53. Week 1 starts on Monday, 1999-01-04.
MAXIFS function
<bookmarkvalue>MAXIFS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>maximum;satisfying conditions</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="maxifshead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcmaxifs.xhp">MAXIFS</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="maxifsdes">Returns the maximum of the values of cells in a range that meets multiple criteria in multiple ranges.</variable></ahelp>
MAXIFS(<embedvar href="text/scalc/01/exdatastatfunc.xhp#args" markup="ignore"/>)
<emph>FuncRange</emph> – required argument. A range of cells, a name of a named range or a label of a column or a row containing values for calculating the maximum.
<item type="input">=MAXIFS(B2:B6;B2:B6;"<35")</item>
Calculates the maximum of values of the range B2:B6 that are greater than or equal to 20. Returns 35. The fifth row does not meet the criterion.
<item type="input">=MAXIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">=20";C2:C6;"<90")</item>
Calculates the maximum of values of the range C2:C6 that are lower than 90 and correspond to cells of the B2:B6 range with values greater than or equal to 20. Returns 85, because the fourth and fifth rows do not meet at least one criterion.
<item type="input">=MAXIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">"MIN(B2:B6);B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the maximum of values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all values of the range B2:B6 except its minimum and maximum. Returns 190, because only the fourth row meet the criteria.
<item type="input">=MAXIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;"pen.*";B2:B6;"<="MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the maximum of values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all cells of the A2:A6 range starting with "pen" and to all cells of the B2:B6 range except its maximum. Returns 85, because only the third row meets all criteria.
If you need to change a criterion easily, you may want to specify it in a separate cell and use a reference to this cell in the condition of the MAXIFS function. For example, the above function can be rewritten as follows:
<item type="input">=MAXIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;E2".*";B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
If E2 = "pen", the function returns 65, because the reference to the cell is substituted with its content.
MINIFS function
<bookmarkvalue>MINIFS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>minimum;satisfying conditions</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="minifshead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcminifs.xhp">MINIFS</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="minifsdes">Returns the minimum of the values of cells in a range that meets multiple criteria in multiple ranges.</variable></ahelp>
<emph>FuncRange</emph> – required argument. A range of cells, a name of a named range or a label of a column or a row containing values for calculating the minimum.
<item type="input">=MINIFS(B2:B6;B2:B6;"<35")</item>
Calculates the minimum of values of the range B2:B6 that are lower than or equal to 20. Returns 17.
<item type="input">=MINIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">=20";C2:C6;">90")</item>
Calculates the minimum of values of the range C2:C6 that are lower than 90 and correspond to cells of the B2:B6 range with values greater than or equal to 20. Returns 190.
<item type="input">=MINIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">"MIN(B2:B6);B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the minimum of values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all values of the range B2:B6 except its minimum and minimum. Returns 65.
<item type="input">=MINIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;".*book";B2:B6;"<="MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the minimum of values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all cells of the A2:A6 range starting with "pen" and to all cells of the B2:B6 range except its minimum. Returns 180.
If you need to change a criterion easily, you may want to specify it in a separate cell and use a reference to this cell in the condition of the MINIFS function. For example, the above function can be rewritten as follows:
<item type="input">=MINIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;".*"E2;B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
If E2 = "book", the function returns 180, because the reference to the cell is substituted with its content.
MINUTE

<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCMINUTE">Calculates the minute for an internal time value.</ahelp> The minute is returned as a number between 0 and 59.

<item type="input">=MINUTE(8.999)</item> returns 58
<item type="input">=MINUTE(8.9999)</item> returns 59
<item type="input">=MINUTE(NOW())</item> returns the current minute value.

NETWORKDAYS.INTL
<bookmarkvalue>NETWORKDAYS.INTL function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="networkdaysintl"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcnetworkdays.intl.xhp">NETWORKDAYS.INTL</link></variable>
<ahelp hid=".">Returns the number of workdays between a start date and an end date. There are options to define weekend days and holidays. The optional weekend parameter (or a string) can be used to define the weekend days (or the non-working days in each week). Also, optionally, the user can define a holiday list. The weekend days and user-defined holidays are not counted as working days.</ahelp>
<emph>StartDate</emph> is the date from when the calculation is carried out. If the start date is a workday, the day is included in the calculation.
<emph>EndDate</emph> is the date up until when the calculation is carried out. If the end date is a workday, the day is included in the calculation.
How many workdays fall between December 15, 2016 and January 14, 2017? Let the start date be located in C3 and the end date in D3. Cells F3 to J3 contain five (5) holidays for Christmas and New Year in date format: December 24, 2016; December 25, 2016; December 26, 2016; December 31, 2016; and January 1, 2017.
<item type="input">=NETWORKDAYS.INTL(C3;D3;;F3:J3)</item> returns 21 workdays with default for weekend days.
<item type="input">=NETWORKDAYS.INTL(C3;D3;11;F3:J3)</item> returns 24 workdays with Sunday only weekends.
Alternatively, use the weekend string “0000001” to define Sunday as the non-working day of every week.
<item type="input">=NETWORKDAYS.INTL(C3;D3;“0000001”;F3:J3)</item> returns 24 workdays with Sunday only weekend.
The function can be used without the two optional parameters – weekday and holidays – by leaving them out:
<item type="input">=NETWORKDAYS.INTL(C3;D3)</item> gives 22 working days.
NETWORKDAYS
<bookmarkvalue>NETWORKDAYS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>NETWORKDAYSEXCEL2003 function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="networkdays"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcnetworkdays.xhp">NETWORKDAYS</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDAAIFUNCNETWORKDAYS">Returns the number of workdays between a <emph>start date</emph> and an <emph>end date</emph>. Holidays can be deducted.</ahelp>
NETWORKDAYS(StartDate; EndDate [; [ Holidays ] [; Workdays ] ])
<emph>Holidays</emph> is an optional list of holidays. These are non-working days. Enter a cell range in which the holidays are listed individually.
<emph>Workdays</emph> is an optional list of number values defining standard work week. This list starts by Sunday, workdays are indicated by zero and non-working days by non-zero value.
How many workdays fall between 2001-12-15 and 2002-01-15? The start date is located in C3 and the end date in D3. Cells F3 to J3 contain the following Christmas and New Year holidays: "2001-12-24", "2001-12-25", "2001-12-26", "2001-12-31", "2002-01-01".
<item type="input">=NETWORKDAYS(C3;D3;F3:J3)</item> returns 17 workdays.
How many workdays fall between September 12nd and 25th in 2016 if only Mondays, Tuesdays and Wednesdays are considered as workdays?
<item type="input">=NETWORKDAYS(DATE(2016;9;12); DATE(2016;9;25); ; {1;0;0;0;1;1;1})</item> returns 6 workdays.
NOW

<variable id="now"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcnow.xhp">NOW</link></variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCJETZT">Returns the computer system date and time.</ahelp> The value is updated when you recalculate the document or each time a cell value is modified.
NOW()
NOW is a function without arguments.
<item type="input">=NOW()-A1</item> returns the difference between the date in A1 and now. Format the result as a number.
NUMBERVALUE
<bookmarkvalue>NUMBERVALUE function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="datevalue">        <link href="text/scalc/01/funcnumbervalue.xhp">NUMBERVALUE</link>      </variable>
<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCNUMBERVALUE">Convert text to number, in a locale-independent way.</ahelp>
Constraints: LEN(decimalseparator) = 1, decimalseparator shall not appear in groupseparator
NUMBERVALUE("Text" [;decimalseparator [;groupseparator]])
<emph>Text</emph> is a valid number expression and must be entered with quotation marks.
<emph>decimalseparator</emph> (optional) defines the character used as the decimal separator.
<emph>groupseparator</emph> (optional) defines the character(s) used as the group separator.
<item type="input">=NUMBERVALUE("123.456";".";",")</item> yields 123.456
Function OPTBARRIER
<bookmarkvalue>OPTBARRIER function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="optbrarrierh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcoptbarrier.xhp" name="OPTBARRIER">OPTBARRIER</link></variable>
<variable id="variable name"><ahelp hid=".">Returns the pricing for a barrier option, calculated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model.</ahelp></variable>
OPTBARRIER(Spot; Volatility; Rate; Foreign Rate; Maturity; Strike; LowerBarrier; UpperBarrier; Rebate; PutCall; InOut; BarrierMonitoring [; Greek])
<emph>Strike</emph> is the strike price of the option and should be non-negative.
<emph>Rebate</emph> is the amount of money to be paid at maturity if the barrier is hit.
<variable id="optputcall"><emph>Put or Call</emph> is a string that defines whether the option is a put (“p”) or a call (“c”).</variable>
<input>=OPTBARRIER(30;0.2;0.06;0;1;40;25;0;0;"c";"o";"c")</input> returns the value 0.4243.
<input>=OPTBARRIER(50;0.4;0.05;0;0.5;65;0;80;0;"p";"o";"c";"e")</input> returns the value 10.1585.
Function OPTPROBHIT
<bookmarkvalue>OPTPROBHIT function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="optprobhith1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcoptprobhit.xhp" name="OPTPROBHIT">OPTPROBHIT</link></variable>
<variable id="variable name"><ahelp hid=".">Returns the probability that an asset hits a predetermined barrier price, assuming that the stock price can be modeled as a process S that follows the stochastic differential equation</ahelp></variable>, as follows.
<image src="media/helpimg/scfuncopt01.svg" id="imgid211575078735993" width="197.38334px" height="51.2125px"><alt id="altid401575078735994">OPTPROBHIT equation</alt></image>
<literal>µ</literal> is the asset’s percentage drift, <literal>vol</literal> is the percentage volatility of the stock, and <literal>dW</literal> is a random sample drawn from a normal distribution with a zero mean. <literal>W</literal> is a Wiener process or Brownian motion.
OPTPROBHIT(Spot; Volatility; Drift; Maturity; LowerBarrier; UpperBarrier)
<variable id="optdrift"><emph>Drift</emph> is the annual stock price percentage drift rate (µ in the above formula). The value is expressed as a decimal (for example, enter 15% as 0.15).</variable>
<variable id="optstrike"><emph>Strike</emph> is the strike price of the option and should be non-negative.</variable>
<input>=OPTPROBHIT(30;0.2;0.3;1;0;40)</input>  returns the value 0.6119.
<input>=OPTPROBHIT(70;0.3;0.1;0.5;60;0)</input>  returns the value 0.4239.
Function OPTPROBINMONEY
<bookmarkvalue>OPTPROBINMONEY function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="optprobinmoneyh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcoptprobinmoney.xhp" name="OPTPROBINMONEY">OPTPROBINMONEY</link></variable>
<variable id="variable name"><ahelp hid=".">Returns the probability that an asset will end up between two barrier levels at maturity, assuming that the stock price can be modeled as a process S that follows the stochastic differential equation</ahelp></variable>, as follows.
<image src="media/helpimg/scfuncopt01.svg" id="imgid211575078735993" width="197.38334px" height="51.2125px"><alt id="altid401575078735994">OPTPROBINMONEY equation</alt></image>
If the optional <emph>Strike</emph> and <emph>PutCall</emph> arguments are included, then
For a call option, the function returns the probability that the asset will end up between <emph>Strike</emph> and <emph>UpperBarrier</emph>.
For a put option, the function returns the probability that the asset will end up between <emph>LowerBarrier</emph> and <emph>Strike</emph>.
The function ignores the possibility of knock-out before maturity.
OPTPROBINMONEY(Spot; Volatility; Drift; Maturity; LowerBarrier; UpperBarrier [; Strike [; PutCall]])
<input>=OPTPROBINMONEY(30;0.2;0.1;1;0;50)</input> returns the value 0.9844.
<input>=OPTPROBINMONEY(70;0.3;0.15;1;60;0;80;"p")</input> returns the value 0.3440.
OPTTOUCH
<bookmarkvalue>OPTTOUCH function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="opttouchh1"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcopttouch.xhp" name="functionopttouch">OPTTOUCH</link></variable>
<ahelp hid=".">Returns the pricing of a touch / no-touch option, calculated using the Black-Scholes option pricing model.</ahelp>
For relevant background information, visit the <link href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Option(finance)" name="optionfinance">Options (finance)</link> and <link href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black–Scholesmodel" name="blackscholes">Black-Scholes</link> model Wikipedia pages.
Further information about touch / no-touch options may be found on many financial websites.
OPTTOUCH(Spot; Volatility; Rate; ForeignRate; Maturity; LowerBarrier; UpperBarrier; ForeignDomestic; InOut; BarrierMonitoring [; Greek])
<variable id="optspot"><emph>Spot</emph> is the price / value of the underlying asset and should be greater than 0.0.</variable>
<variable id="optvolat"><emph>Volatility</emph> is the annual percentage volatility of the underlying asset expressed as a decimal (for example, enter 30% as 0.3). The value should be greater than 0.0.</variable>
<variable id="optrate"><emph>Rate</emph> is the continuously compounded interest rate. This is a percentage expressed as a decimal (for example, enter 40% as 0.4).</variable>
<variable id="optfrate"><emph>ForeignRate</emph> is the continuously compounded foreign interest rate. This is a percentage expressed as a decimal (for example, enter 50% as 0.5).</variable>
<variable id="optmaturity"><emph>Maturity</emph> is the time to maturity of the option, in years, and should be non-negative.</variable>
<variable id="optlowbar"><emph>LowerBarrier</emph> is the predetermined lower barrier price; set to zero for no lower barrier.</variable>
<variable id="optupbar"><emph>UpperBarrier</emph> is the predetermined upper barrier price; set to zero for no upper barrier.</variable>
<variable id="optdomestic"><emph>ForeignDomestic</emph> is a string that defines whether the option pays domestic (“d”) or foreign (“f”) currency.</variable>
<variable id="optinout"><emph>InOut</emph> is a string that defines whether the option is knock-in (“i”) or knock-out (“o”).</variable>
<variable id="optbarmon"><emph>BarrierMonitoring</emph> is a string that defines whether the barrier is monitored continuously (“c”) or only at the end / maturity (“e”).</variable>
<emph>Greek</emph> (optional) is a string argument. If omitted or set to “value”, “v”, “price”, or “p”, then the function simply returns the option price. If another valid string is entered, the function returns price sensitivities (Greeks) to one of the input parameters. The valid options in this case are as follows.
“delta” or “d”.
“gamma” or “g”.
“theta” or “t”.
“vega” or “e”.
“volga” or “o”.
“vanna” or “a”.
“rho” or “r”.
“rhof” or “f”.
<input>=OPTTOUCH(50;0.25;0.05;0;1;0;55;"d";"i";"c")</input>  returns the value 0.6876.
<input>=OPTTOUCH(80;0.2;0.05;0;0.5;60;0;"f";"o";"c";"r")</input>  returns the value 15.5516.
<link href="text/scalc/01/04060103.xhp">Financial Functions Part One</link>
<link href="text/scalc/01/04060119.xhp">Financial Functions Part Two</link>
<link href="text/scalc/01/04060118.xhp">Financial Functions Part Three</link>
RAWSUBTRACT function
<bookmarkvalue>rawsubtract;subtraction</bookmarkvalue>        <bookmarkvalue>RAWSUBTRACT function</bookmarkvalue>
<link href="text/scalc/01/funcrawsubtract.xhp">RAWSUBTRACT</link>
<ahelp hid=".">Subtracts a set of numbers and gives the result without eliminating small roundoff errors.</ahelp>
RAWSUBTRACT(Minuend; Subtrahend 1[; Subtrahend 2][; … ;[ Subtrahend 254]])
<emph>Minuend</emph> is a number or a reference to a cell containing a number.
<emph>Subtrahend 1[; Subtrahend 2][; ... ;[ Subtrahend 254]]</emph> are numbers or references to cells containing numbers.
The function should be called with at least two parameters.
<input>=RAWSUBTRACT(0.987654321098765, 0.9876543210987)</input> returns 6.53921361504217E-14
<input>=RAWSUBTRACT(0.987654321098765)</input> returns Err:511 (Missing variable) because RAWSUBTRACT requires a minimum of two numbers.
REGEX Function
<bookmarkvalue>REGEX function</bookmarkvalue>            <bookmarkvalue>regular expressions;extracting in spreadsheets</bookmarkvalue>            <bookmarkvalue>regular expressions;REGEX function</bookmarkvalue>
<link href="text/scalc/01/funcregex.xhp" name="function REGEX">REGEX</link>
<variable id="funcregexdesc"><ahelp hid=".">Matches and extracts or optionally replaces text using regular expressions.</ahelp></variable>
REGEX( Text ; Expression [ ; [ Replacement ] [ ; Flags|Occurrence ] ] )
<emph>Text</emph>: A text or reference to a cell where the regular expression is to be applied.
<emph>Expression</emph>: A text representing the regular expression, using <link href="http://userguide.icu-project.org/strings/regexp" name="ICU REGEXP">ICU regular expressions</link>. If there is no match and <emph>Replacement</emph> is not given, #N/A is returned.
<emph>Replacement</emph>: Optional. The replacement text and references to capture groups. If there is no match, <emph>Text</emph> is returned unmodified.
<emph>Flags</emph>: Optional. "g" replaces all matches of <emph>Expression</emph> in <emph>Text</emph>, not extracted. If there is no match, <emph>Text</emph> is returned unmodified.
<emph>Occurrence</emph>: Optional. Number to indicate which match of <emph>Expression</emph> in <emph>Text</emph> is to be extracted or replaced. If there is no match and <emph>Replacement</emph> is not given, #N/A is returned. If there is no match and <emph>Replacement</emph> is given, <emph>Text</emph> is returned unmodified. If <emph>Occurrence</emph> is 0, <emph>Text</emph> is returned unmodified.
<item type="input">=REGEX("123456ABCDEF";"[:digit:]";"Z")</item>  returns "Z23456ABCDEF", where the first match of a digit is replaced by "Z".
<item type="input">=REGEX("123456ABCDEF";"[:digit:]";"Z";"g")</item>  returns "ZZZZZZABCDEF", where all digits were replaced by "Z".
<item type="input">=REGEX("123456ABCDEF";"[126]";"";"g")</item>  returns "345ABCDEF", where any occurrence of "1", "2" or "6" is replaced by the empty string, thus deleted.
<item type="input">=REGEX("axbxcxd";".x";;2)</item>  returns "bx", the second match of ".x".
<item type="input">=REGEX("axbxcxd";"(.)x";"$1y";2)</item>  returns "axbycxd", the second match of "(.)x" (i.e. "bx") replaced with the captured group of one character (i.e. "b") followed by "y".
<link href="text/shared/01/02100001.xhp" name="regex lists">List of regular expressions</link>
<link href="http://userguide.icu-project.org/strings/regexp" name="ICU REGEXP">ICU regular expressions</link>
REPLACEB Function
<bookmarkvalue>REPLACEB Function</bookmarkvalue>            <bookmarkvalue>replace text;REPLACEB Function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="replaceb"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcreplaceb.xhp" name="replaceb">REPLACEB</link></variable>
<variable id="variable name"><ahelp hid=".">Returns text where an old text is replaced with a new text, using byte positions.</ahelp></variable>
REPLACEB( Text ; Position ; Length ; NewText )
<emph>Text</emph>: A text expression or reference to a cell containing a text expression in which the characters are to be replaced.
<emph>Position</emph>: the character position from which text is to be replaced.
<emph>Length</emph>: the number of characters to be replaced.
<emph>NewText</emph>: the text to be inserted.
<input>=REPLACEB("ᄩᄔᄕᄜᄝᄞᄠᄢᄣᄫᄬᄭᄮᄯᄲᄶ";4;1;"ab")</input> returns "ᄩ abᄕᄜᄝᄞᄠᄢᄣᄫᄬᄭᄮᄯᄲᄶ" .

SKEWP function

SUMIFS function
<bookmarkvalue>SUMIFS function</bookmarkvalue>  <bookmarkvalue>sum;satisfying conditions</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="sumifshead"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcsumifs.xhp">SUMIFS</link></variable> function
<ahelp hid="."><variable id="sumifsdes">Returns the sum of the values of cells in a range that meets multiple criteria in multiple ranges.</variable></ahelp>
<emph>FuncRange</emph> – required argument. It is a range of cells, a name of a named range or a label of a column or a row containing values for calculating the sum.
<item type="input">=SUMIFS(B2:B6;B2:B6;">=20")</item>
Calculates the sum of values of the range B2:B6 that are greater than or equal to 20. Returns 75, because the fifth row does not meet the criterion.
<item type="input">=SUMIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">=20";C2:C6;">70")</item>
Calculates the sum of values of the range C2:C6 that are greater than 70 and correspond to cells of the B2:B6 range with values  greater than or equal to 20. Returns 275, because the second and the fifth rows do not meet at least one criterion.
<item type="input">=SUMIFS(C2:C6;B2:B6;">"MIN(B2:B6);B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the sum of values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all values of the range B2:B6 except its minimum and maximum. Returns 255, because the third and the fifth rows do not meet at least one criterion.
<item type="input">=SUMIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;"pen.*";B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
Calculates the sum of values of the range C2:C6 that correspond to all cells of the A2:A6 range starting with "pen" and to all cells of the B2:B6 range except its maximum. Returns 65, because only second row meets all criteria.
If you need to change a criterion easily, you may want to specify it in a separate cell and use a reference to this cell in the condition of the SUMIFS function. For example, the above function can be rewritten as follows:
<item type="input">=SUMIFS(C2:C6;A2:A6;E2".*";B2:B6;"<"MAX(B2:B6))</item>
SWITCH function
<bookmarkvalue>SWITCH function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="switchfunct"><link href="text/scalc/01/funcswitch.xhp" name="switch">SWITCH</link></variable>
<variable id="functionswitch"><ahelp hid=".">SWITCH compares <emph>expression</emph> with <emph>value1</emph> to <emph>valuen</emph> and returns the result belonging to the first value that equals expression. If there is no match and defaultresult is given, that will be returned.</ahelp></variable>
SWITCH(expression; value1; result1[; value2; result2][; ... ; [value127; result127][; defaultresult]])
If you choose not to specify a default result, 127 value / result pairs may be entered as parameters. If you choose to include a default result at the end of the list of parameters, then only 126 value / result pairs may be entered.
<emph>expression</emph> is a text, numeric, logical or date input or reference to a cell.
<emph>value1, value2, ...</emph>  is any value or reference to a cell. Each value must have a result given.
<emph>result1, result2, ...</emph> is any value or reference to a cell.
<emph>defaultresult</emph>: any value or reference to a cell that is returned when there is no match.
If no <emph>value</emph> equals <emph>expression</emph> and no default result is given, a #N/A error is returned.
<input>=SWITCH(MONTH(A3),1,"January",2,"February",3,"March","No match")</input> returns "January" when A3 contains a date in January, "February" when A3 contains a date in February , etc...
TEXTJOIN function
<bookmarkvalue>TEXTJOIN function</bookmarkvalue>
<variable id="textjoinfunct"><link href="text/scalc/01/functextjoin.xhp" name="textjoinfunction">TEXTJOIN</link></variable>
<variable id="textjoinfunction"><ahelp hid=".">Concatenates one or more strings, and uses delimiters between them.</ahelp></variable>
TEXTJOIN( delimiter, skipempty, String 1[; String 2][; … ;[String 253]] )
<emph>delimiter</emph> is a text string and can be a range.
<emph>skipempty</emph> is a logical (TRUE or FALSE, 1 or 0) argument. When TRUE, empty strings will be ignored.
<emph>String 1[; String 2][; … ;[String 253]]</emph> are strings,  references to cells or to cell ranges of strings.
Ranges are traversed row by row (from top to bottom).
If <emph>delimiter</emph> is a range, the range need not be of the same size as the number of strings to be joined.
If there are more delimiters than strings to be joined, not all delimiters will be used.
If there are less delimiters than strings to be joined, the delimiters will be used again from the start.
<input>=TEXTJOIN(" ",TRUE, "Here", "comes", "the", "sun")</input> returns "Here comes the sun" with space character as delimiter and empty strings are ignored.
if A1:B2 contains "Here", "comes", "the", "sun" respectively, <input>=TEXTJOIN("-",TRUE,A1:B2)</input> returns "Here-comes-the-sun" with dash character as delimiter and empty strings are ignored.

TIME(Hour; Minute; Second)

<item type="input">=TIME(0;0;0)</item> returns 00:00:00

<ahelp hid="HIDFUNCZEITWERT">TIMEVALUE returns the internal time number from a text enclosed by quotes and which may show a possible time entry format.</ahelp>
The internal number indicated as a decimal is the result of the date system used under $[officename] to calculate date entries.
If the text string also includes a year, month, or day, TIMEVALUE only returns the fractional part of the conversion.
TIMEVALUE("Text")
<emph>Text</emph> is a valid time expression and must be entered in quotation marks.
